de dolor anciene en aucun membre	than the old ones in any limb.
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain arises in any limb, be it from sitting or injury, and this pain persists for a long time, and the medical cure proves useless, then it is appropriate to cauterize using the cautery called "poins," or to cauterize according to the length of the limb, its breadth and weakness, its toughness and flexibility, and its location of torsion and pain. If it is cured after the first cautery, that is well; if not, repeat the procedure. Indeed, it is customary to perform subsequent cauteries on the adjacent part of the limb so that you can make the cauteries until the patient is cured.
de meselerie	When pain arises in any limb, be it from sitting or injury, and this pain persists for a long time, and the medical cure proves useless, then it is appropriate to cauterize using the cautery called "poins," or to cauterize according to the length of the limb, its breadth and weakness, its toughness and flexibility, and its location of torsion and pain. If it is cured after the first cautery, that is well; if not, repeat the procedure. Indeed, it is customary to perform subsequent cauteries on the adjacent part of the limb so that you can make the cauteries until the patient is cured.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The disease of mesentery is never cured by cautery, and the same is true of the diseases which arise from the corruption of phlegm and melancholy. When you see that the disease has begun, take warning; if it is cured according to what we have said in the preceding division, and if you do not delay, you will doubt that the corruption has spread throughout the whole sickness, and so you must make five cauteries on the head: that is to say, one on the top of the head, and one at the front of the jaw at the end of the beard; and two on the two corners, and one behind the ear; and leave the hand as long as the cauteries are going on until the bones are reached, and as long as the pus comes out forcefully so that the vapors of the humors can escape; and cauterize the head according to what is seen before you.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the moisture is sparse throughout; and it persists openly, as you must know, that you must cauterize from these cauteries which we have mentioned or chief, namely: cauterize on the summit of the nose, and two on the eyebrow of the eye, three on the eyebrow of the shoulder, one large on the hip and one elsewhere, two on the two thumbs, two on the wrists, and two on the tendons of the elbows, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the fossae of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are behind the calcaneus, that you do not burn them; and in no way perform cautery on the bone of the ankle or on the bone of the stomach or on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And as many as you make cautery, the more aid you do, and the more it helps; and as many as the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as when he feels it, because the flesh is already corrupted. It is necessary that the cautery be great and small according to the limbs and joints, as you do in handling herbs. After treatment with flour several times with honey and other treatments until it is healed.
de enfleure	of swelling
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling occurs in any limb and is cured by medicines, oils, and plasters, and is not completely healed, then it is necessary to perform cautery on the limb according to the size and severity of the swelling; and let the burn penetrate deeply into the flesh. Then cure with unguents until the swelling is healed. And never perform cautery on the hand, foot, or back, at the opening of a nerve that causes the limb to move, or if it is bony swelling; and in no case should anything interfere with it except one who is skilled in limbs and the issues of the moving nerves and bones.
de albaras	When swelling occurs in any limb and is cured by medicines, oils, and plasters, and is not completely healed, then it is necessary to perform cautery on the limb according to the size and severity of the swelling; and let the burn penetrate deeply into the flesh. Then cure with unguents until the swelling is healed. And never perform cautery on the hand, foot, or back, at the opening of a nerve that causes the limb to move, or if it is bony swelling; and in no case should anything interfere with it except one who is skilled in limbs and the issues of the moving nerves and bones.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is present, and medicines are of no avail, then it is necessary to cauterize with a needle a little deep, according to the amount of flesh involved, until the burn is solid; and then cure with flour of times, lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, with colon and alum, a part of each; mix them all together and bind them with a cloth, and keep it covered until healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure for fistula by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When the fistula starts, and you see it stop, if you cauterize at the cautery that seems like a circle, surround the fistula entirely.  And whatever people say about making the cautery in the middle of the fistula; in my opinion that is not good, because I fear that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen several times that it is better to cauterize around the circumference, at the cautery which is called the "circle", as we have said about other cauteries.</start_of_turn>
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot be measured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When anyone has a disease called "adubelati," and it lingers without healing or because of its excessive heat or because of the hardness of the patient when decrepit (that is, too old), and there is little blood left, or because of weakness; and you see it haste to heal: then cauterize around the mouth of small cauteries by pricking; afterwards leave it alone. For it will haste to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it turning pale with all the cautery, if the burn is large:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And put your hand in the middle of this disease which is called "adubelati" as long as the cauteries have perceived the pain, and be like those cauteries that the patient feels depart in some part as long as the process of putrefaction is joyful. After that cure until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The fire cautery. Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	The fire cautery. Another method for disease which is called "corrodens" is nothing but the wasting away of a limb, because it causes the limb to be as brittle as burnt straw. If you see this disease in a patient who can endure fire cautery, then singe out the nails cautiously, small and large, as much as is necessary according to the nature of the disease; after which cauterize all parts until you have eradicated all corruption, leaving nothing but sound bone. Then leave it for two days, and put on the cauterized limb, anoint with oil until the charred portions are ossified, and all the corruption is gone. After the cure of the wounds that ensue. And if after two days you see that the wound has not healed, repeat the cautery on that which remains corrupt. This wasting away is never cured by medical treatment alone, but every kind of fire cautery is of more great benefit. As I have already said in the division: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	from pores that come as pieces
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times it happens that by a sudden discharge of humours a disease arises which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and is a great and bloody matter. And the cautery of this disease is as follows. That is, cautery of fire and cautery of hot water. The cautery of fire is that you should grasp the hair as though it were a pin of wool, and make it of fine iron to the measure that it can penetrate the clot of all parts, and that there be subtle margins; after that put all around the clot, and hold your hand tightly around the clot until it comes to the front of the clot; and leave it thus for two days until it begins to soften by putrefaction; then make an embolus of wild mallow bruised with oil, and leave the embolus on all night, and close the wound carefully and remove the sutures from their roots. Then cure the wound by applying charcoal as long as it is sane.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are converted by discharge of humours from the head and hands and in the feet, if you must do so, bring a cautery of hot water; and this is partly in manner: take a bowl of lead or iron, or a pin of wool, and put it on the clot and the underlay; that is, put nails on the edges. And put the bowl on so that it encloses everything, then put a little of warm oil on it, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand by turning so that the margin of the bowl comes to the root of the clot, and can find the hot water going deep down to the root; and offer the patient a little of the hot water an hour; then leave it thus, and it will drain out all at its roots. Thus do another, until you have removed all that is at the head, and then cure the wounds that have arisen from charcoal.
li cure dou trembler	you cure the tremor.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some tremble from cold, or from quartan fever or from any other cause, if you make for them three or four cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades, and one cautery or pinch on the stomach at the olive cautery, if you leave them to tremble, they will haste the recovery from the cold sickness.
des pustules puans	When some tremble from cold, or from quartan fever or from any other cause, if you make for them three or four cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades, and one cautery or pinch on the stomach at the olive cautery, if you leave them to tremble, they will haste the recovery from the cold sickness.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Whenever the body is bathed in pus or boils appear, which come from corrupted matters, if you make the first incision when they appear, make a superficial incision with a needle of myrtle, so that the tip grasps the fire or with long aristology root, or with the lenticular cautery. And never should you begin the incisions until they appear, following this method, for otherwise they will not go forward but are broken by the discharge from which they come, and are cured; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is severed.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	There have often been great discharges of blood from the artery that is severed at the wound that comes from the surgeon, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is a great grief thing to extend it.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And whenever this happens to anyone, if you are in a hurry to put your thumb on the wound of the vein, and you strain too much without being appeased by the blood, and that no blood comes out any more; then put the olive cautery on the wound several small and large times until they are all red; and take hold, that is to say, big or small as the wound and the limb allow, since the artery is clear, and put the cautery on that vein or hold your thumb there, and hold the cautery as long as it is not fixed.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spurts out when you take your thumb away from the vein, and the cautery is finished, take hold urgently of another cautery that is on the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And cease not to do this one after the other until the limb is fully extended; and beware that thou dost not touch the nerve which is below, and that no other mischief arise upon the patient; and that when without drawing blood from an artery, one cannot well fill himself up again as when the artery is large, save by one of the three ways that we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not otherwise treated, or by tightly tying with thread or by medicines placed upon it which have power to fill up blood; and let it be bound and strained afterwards.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will bring about a lasting restoration of the limb except by the strict draping of cloths or the application of hot things upon it, or other similar things, if it does not profit thereby in some way.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and there is no remedy or medicine present, if he must put his thumb on the wound of the vein as we have said, and keep it still until it is healed from under the wound and from under the vein; and do not move it, but moisten it often with cold water so that it be cold as long as the limb is frozen and swollen and healed; and make inquiries of him concerning the things which he must have to cauterize and medicate.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	Now we have said or first chapter that every disease in which it is necessary to cauterize with fire, or with burning medicine, and the ointment and the causes and the instruments and the forms of cauterization; and I put this chapter from the head down to the toes, and I will speak of this chapter in the same way as we have found it more lightly in this way.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus, as I begin this chapter, it is necessary to say, my dear friend, that in this chapter there is more peril and fear than in all the previous cauteries, and for this reason it is necessary to take greater caution
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you that you should not act rashly. For from many people come cures. If they come from those who have suffered so much with their illness that they move lightly from the fear of their suffering, and from the greatness of their malice; from these things we must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And from these there are those who will tell you: "Wait, I am well enough"; and the illness is desperate. It is not fitting that you should trust only those who come to you who have this manner, but put more great caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not foolishly believe more than reasonably of what you are certain, and of what you have taken and lost; and use prognostication and indication in the treatment of your patients so that salvation may be either converted or obtained; and this will help you to acquire renown, glory, and memory in the long run.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, our Sirs, you must take good understanding and diligence, and if you yearn to be inspired by the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter in dividing by chapters, according to what is before or the chapter of cautery, that I have devised from the head to the toes, because you will find it more readily what you have to master.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Or I have commanded this chapter to be divided into chapters, according to what precedes or the chapter of cautery, that I have devised from the head to the toes, because you will more easily find what you have to learn.</start_of_turn>
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	The disease often comes out of the belly of a child, and when the bath is too hot the head of the child is strained; and never comes from a known cause except that one does not know it.</start_of_turn
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never saw such a disease depart as quickly as in summer; and for all that I have seen, it is better to leave the work in parts rather than to risk it.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw that in childhood, when the shoulder was dislocated, the head would swell up so much that it could not bear; and it was believed that the moisture was too great, and when it is gathered between the bone and the cartilage, between the shoulder and the bone; and when such moisture is between the shoulder and the bone, and the incision is small, that you must make a wide incision; and be as long as two fingers, until the moisture is gone.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper and the incision is larger, if you make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:

If on the first incision the instrument which is called the "cultellaire", which is very well chiselled on one side and soft on the other, does not penetrate, it is like this: drive the chisel towards the marrow at the head, and the soft part towards the bone, and hold it until the incision reaches the marrow, and then proceed in the middle incision until the other side is reached; then drain the blood equally, express the marrow out of the wound; then place in the wound a patch of coarse cotton, and cover with damp cloths soaked in wine and oil and wool, and keep still until the sutures are removed; and at the third hour remove the dressing and administer strong poultices of cold water, then treat with basic ointment with rose oil and other remedies for wounds, until they are healed.

de l’estoupement des oreilles	From the swelling of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses. Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When there is a piece of wood or other foreign object in the ear that does not fit into the ear, do not put it into the ear. Many times this cure comes out by itself; and if it does not come out, you must perform an extraction with needles, as this is the shape:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out by itself, that is good; if not, you must perform an extraction with a blunt needle of small double curvature; and if it does not come out with that, take a grip of the hair of the ear with your thumb and index finger, and pull out whatever is around the needle without causing any damage; then the pain will vanish, for often it comes out by itself as we have said; and if it does not come out partly, take hold of the hair with your thumb and index finger, and put on no instrument that might cause damage, and put a little cotton around; then press on the grip above the ear or whatever it is, and the pain will vanish.

When the ear aches, then the patient must use a wet compress first and fill the ear with much cotton wool. And if the pain persists in this ear or in the other, if it leaps for this, that is good. En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the tooth, if it is of small root, as like a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of great root we must feel it, if it threatens extraction of teeth; and that is the lightest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ear, when you have cured as we have said in the division or treated with distillations, and the cure does not help, if you must look at the ear in the sun: if there are no worms seen, if you do treatments for subtle worms, and if they are not seen, take the tweezers that are like this:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if it is necessary to open the ear, make the opening wide and deep. Then take the needle according to the amount of suffering of the patient, and pierce through to the bottom; do this often until you see it issue. And if it does not obey, if I press around the cotton wool as I have said concerning the stone; and if it does not come out, if we have said, give distillations that the ancients have proved useful in the excision of worms, and you will find them or treat them with distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all these instruments, this is the form as you see.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And if it is of silver or gold, cut off the tip of the earlobe, about the size of small grains of pepper, and above that pour oil through the distiller; and press with this instrument of gold well made for this purpose. If you see take a scraper and wrap around the end of the awl cotton; then pour in your oil or juice, and whatever you see of your medicines in the cotton, and the cotton be in the ear; then pour in from the scraper to the end of the cotton, and press gently until the oil is distilled or the ear is emptied. And let the patient feel within, and if the distillations are too cold, for the medicine will not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	From the swelling of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some imperfection in their ears; and the same thing happens as they grow up from wounds or tumors that grow inside the ear, for these stampings never come out of the ear if they are not seen; and never does any part of the ear depart without being seen.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	When they come out of the ear, if they are not seen, it is a sign of great suffering in many conditions, and in this case it is seen that you put the painful ear in the sun; and look inside: if you see the opening clearly, if the tumor has completely filled this cavity, this is its form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And either be blunt or pointed before and behind all around, if it does not bleed the ear; if the opening is of a tumor or a piece of the ear, if you have subtle piercings and hold it lightly, as long as the tumor is completely bony.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If the ear opening is inflamed, take a slender needle and pass a little of the burnish into the fire, then apply it to the ear. If you feel the inflammation which the patient feels at the ear, pierce slightly, and keep that you do not damage the nerves of the ear; then put in the ear a patch according to the size of the hole, and pour in the unguent Egyptian.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not do anything until the wound is healed; or take a patch and pour in rose-water, and sprinkle on powdered vitriol; and if you see the ear flee, you may know that you have pulled out the patch and put in another patch made of rose oil and beeswax, until the swelling is bony; then cure it until it is healed
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	If blood comes from the wound, plunge a sponge and cover it with cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other treatments which will stop the bleeding of the blood that comes from the wound such as distillations.
de la char des papieres	De la char des papiers.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Hence it often comes to pass with paper that when it is moist and dry, if you stretch it out with tongs and pinches its root, and put out the brittle vitriol; then take out the broken piece.</start_of_turn>
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without remedy, if the lenticular cautery is applied too late after the incision, it is of little use; and many times repeated, cannot any longer remain rooted at their root; for when they are cauterized by fire, they are burned out and do not return.</start_of_turn
de la gresle	De la gresle.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times come out of papers things that seem to swell in their form and hardness; and for this reason this disease is called "granulinea," and is an assembly of great moisture in the papere below and above; the work is like this: take guard if the granulinea moves from one side to the other, and this is a light matter to know; then make a large incision, then escore the flesh lightly, then take grasp of the tweezers, and close. If you do not close it in the right way, the patient will grieve nothing; and if the split is great, if the assembly has a costure, and cure until it is healed; and if it is small, do not make force, for it will restore itself quickly and leave scars.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the granulinea descends downwards towards the edge of the ear towards the upper part, if you reverse the papere, and extend the granulinea with a grasp, and close and press from one side and the other; and if the papere is pulled out by the incision, this will grieve nothing; and when the granulinea is closed, if you leave the dirty oil, cure the limb of what it leaves scarred until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	from the fat of the hairs
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	The greasy exudate is enclosed in paper tissues, and this is more common in women than in men, and grieves the eyes, and comes out in the morning; it does not tolerate the sight of the sun because the tears hurry out at its eyes; and because of this they lie face down and sleep, and their paper tissues are wet with moisture that swells them and makes them appear covered in exudate. And when you press the area towards your thighs and feel the exudate between your thighs.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	If the patient puts his head in his sound health; then take one drape of linen, and make a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity of exudate from the chest, and put it on him; and press on his thighs from one side and the other, so that the exudate is gathered into the circle; then make an incision in the middle of the moisture at the level of a wide vein, and do not make it any larger than the wound made to the vein; and close the skin as much as you see to the exudate; and in many situations the exudate comes out of the incision, according to the shape of a white piece of fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Pull out all the fatty tumor between your thighs towards your buttocks, and twist your hand to the right and to the left as much as possible; and keep that you do not insert anything into the incision, that you do not go beyond the middle of the moisture, that you do not bleed.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	If the shoulder joint does not spontaneously open at the beginning of the wound, if you expand the wound slightly until it opens; then draw it out as we have said, and moisten the edges with oil and water, and place over it, and strain from the armpit.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there are such people who crush themselves and put on those who are corrupting this moisture that is remaining. Then cure it until it is healed. And if it comes to the limb being cut off because of this, if you cure the abscesses that are surrounding it as much as it is healed.</start_of_turn>
des poilz des papieres	hair of papers</start_of_turn>
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper-like substances grow hair-like, other than their natural state, and are overgrown, if they prick at the eyes, they cause various diseases similar to tears and the softening of paper and gum, until it is the cause of the destruction of the eyes; and the cure is in three ways: either by complete fire cautery, or by medicine according to what is before or alongside the cautery, or by incision and stitching or by sutures, according to what I shall say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must put the patient’s head in your left hand, and turn the paper of the oil to your right hand; if it is converted, that is good; but if not, if there is a needle at any one thread of the paper, either cut the margin of the paper or the hair will grow out from these hairs; and take one thread from below and pass it through the middle of the paper, and turn the paper with the needle; then make on the underside of the paper the paper of the hair, the hair that is overgrown, over the whole expanse, from the great tear to the little; then take out one thread, and put under the paper a little patch of cotton and bandage, and make on the paper a figure like a thrush’s beak, as much as you see the paper that is intended to be elevated.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if there is much paper that has become soft in any part, then make on the whole expanse over the last three lines that you have marked, and from the great tear to the little; and if there is a split at any of the roots of the hair near their natural state in the thickness of a radish, then hold the ointment in one of the two angles of the wound, and then pull it out; then assemble the two layers with a suture of a needle with a thread of fine wool, and wipe away the blood, and leave the excess of the threads on the two corners of all things that are glued, as you see; and if you do not see this, if there is no cure, then leave the suture and the threads for two or three days; and then cure the wound with sutures of dry and constricting things, for the paper is renewed at the bottom of the wound and the assembling of it, but the suture is dry (as they say of the old ones), and this is laborious without fear;
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	If at another time: if you mark the mark of a figure which is as much like the fuelle of mirtle as we have said, as we have often recounted, then two ounces of vinegar should be administered according to the form which is mentioned above.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then hold that which is above down with equal force according to the form which is mentioned above
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you do not have the power to hold the trocars, and the thing is not equal, if you take a needle or if there is a thread, and you hold the mark with the needle; and you take another thread and loop the greater amount of liquid, and the second thread loop the lesser amount, and assemble between your two the threads equally; then hold your hand equally, and hold all the skin above where you have signed, as we have recounted, and assemble the two layers of the wound by sutures, and cure until it is healed; and if there is an abscess at your incision, if you apply cerate and other soothing dressings.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And never has it happened that the hair of the beard has been converted: if you use what we have said about incision; but the costure in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for boils is as follows: convert the beard hair and leave it inside as I have said, then make three boils by art, and three threads as long as the beard and as wide as a palm; and put two threads of two parts or where you hold the hair; then assemble the one and the other securely over what rests on the beard oil, and strain the three boils of two parts forward; and leave it as it is for several days, and the skin that has been strained will rot and decay and will fester, until it heals by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late, if the boil has increased in force, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is closed, and if the beard has fallen out, the hair will no longer prick; and this is the form of the three boils that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you grasp a subtle needle, and there is in it a silken thread of silk and subtle; then gather the threads and know each one from the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm of a long; then order in the chase another subtle thread of silk briefly, and do not tie the knots; then put the patient’s head in its place; and let there be a delay of the sun if the work is completed, for it is a subtle and small work, then withdraw the needle from all the chase at the root of the hair, and make it pierce in the papere hastingly as much as you can until you have treated as much of the hair as its natural position; then withdraw the hair until it comes back to the chase, and keep that hair which is there or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand until the vein has fled from all the chase in the papere with the natural position.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	If the chase is treated and the hair does not come out with it, if you draw out the chase to the end of the thread that you have ordered, until the chase vein comes out through the opening and you see it by the vision of the oil; then if you draw out the chase and the thread, close the oil and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair has returned to its place and the burden has gone; and if the hair is small, if you accompany it with long nails of a natural kind, and be rid of it with that or leave it, until it is elongated and then leave it be.
de la porriture de l’oil	from the corruption of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease which is called 'aleacrati' or the rotting comes to the boil, if there are two methods: one natural, and the other unnatural.  And it comes about by wound, or by cutting or cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the way of working in this is that you make that suture, and dry the flesh, and put in between layers of lint, and keep it until it is healed; and do not do anything except use in the treatment of this things that dry and constrict. For if you do this, if the disease comes back worse than before; but there are things that are softening, as for example, fennel; and alum or salt and seed of lint being cooked, and aquilon oil melted in neither of the oils, and it surrounds a bandage, and treats this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you must take care that it does not heal differently from the way it was before; and this work that we have mentioned is not fierce except for addressing this disease, that it does not return differently from the way it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	From the fire that comes in oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	From the fire that comes in oil, this disease which is commonly called “axacrati” and is natural and accidental. dou soudement de la papiere	And if the ailment comes from a fracture or sprain or burn, if you must make an incision, make it full through the hair of papers; then stretch between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and it must be done according to the form of the ailment, for it is diverse in form, and the wise masters perceive with great insight all sorts of things that must be done to return the limb to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is to be done and the instruments in multiple positions.

de l’ungle de l’oil	De l’ungle de l’oil.

de la bowe de l’oil	De la bowe de l’oil.
