de la piere	De la piere.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already mentioned in the previous chapter the methods of extracting stones, and the medications associated with this; and we mentioned the difference between a retained stone and one that is not, and the signs of each; and when a stone should be removed in size; and in the bladder, and in the kidney. And I will tell you openly and briefly about this.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that a stone that is retained in the bladder is often as painful as when it is expelled; and this is a sign that the stone is breaking from its root, like the pain of a splinter in its subtlety. And it opens gravel, and grinds the patient’s side, and causes them to urinate frequently, and then becomes cold; and from these spurts there is often a discharge of pus. And it is light to cure these spasms until they are about three years old; and it is more painful in old people, and is like a woman in her youth, to those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.</start_of_turn
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the treatment, if it is necessary first to cleanse the patient thoroughly with a catharsis, to drive out all the evil which is in the intestines. For it never fails to obstruct the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the limbs, loosen and move downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and never fails to go out without any trace of its passage; then make him sit between your hands, with his hands resting on his thighs, so that the bladder is completely relaxed downwards; then query and touch again.</start_of_turn>
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in the space, if you hurry immediately to cut above the stone. And if it does not split at the touch of all, if you apply your middle finger oil from your left hand, if the patient is an adult, or your index finger, if the patient is a youth with accomplices; and press it to its foundation, query the stone, and when you feel it with your middle finger, if the urine comes out at the navel of the bladder; then press above your middle finger, and the stone will come out whether you see it cut or not.</start_of_turn>
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the intestines upwards, and with his left hand to grasp the skin which is below the intestines in the part where the size is taken; then insert the sponge covering, as it is formed:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the intestines upwards, and with his left hand to grasp the skin which is below the intestines in the part where the size is taken; then insert the sponge covering, as it is formed:
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And by chance the press if two which is or the foundation, that it leaps forward in work; and threads that there is part stone or there are angles, and margins: if it is grasped to stir; and if there is part which is soft, similar to a gland, round, from which there is little issue.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	If there are angles and margins, make the size greater; and if it does not jump, know that you must draw upon the nails which are as sharp as a file at the head, to grasp the stone if it does not escape; or you may give it a blow with a subtle instrument curved at the head. If you do not know how to handle it, it will become large and loose, and if it does not yield, it is like straining vitriol.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	If there are several stones, grasp the largest at the belly of the bladder first, then hold above, then draw out, and the smaller afterwards if there are more. If it is of great size, cover it with silk and make a greater wound. For in these things three things happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine comes out uncontrollably because his testicles cannot support; but whatever you do to try to drain it, or to remove the nails, as long as you drain it piecemeal.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	When you have finished your work, apply the poultice of incense and aloe and dragon’s blood, and hold it tight, and put on above it a moist bandage soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the burn; then raise the patient up on his heel, and do not loosen the thread until the third joint.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have pulled it out, if there is any blood remaining in the wound from oil and water, then cure it with beeswax ointment and linseed oil, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if blood comes out of the wound after the cautery and corrodings, and swelling of blood in the bladder, and whether it be that the urine is retained, which is known in part as a dry urine: do not leave it in the wound, but drain it out, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and carry it away.</start_of_turn>
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then lift the wound from the water and easily and gently and support it, and help in every way that you can, until it is healed; and it is advised that all the parts that you cure should be bound with threads, and the medicines should be placed on the wound.</start_of_turn
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the passage of the bladder, and it is fixed, and the urine cannot pass; if the physician does what I have said above, then we will hear of the size of this treatment. I have seen this already.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take hold of the forceps according to this shape and be at a right angle with two teeth fixed in one socket:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take one thread and tie it around the bladder near the stone, so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then grasp the forceps lightly in the bladder until it reaches the stone; and turn the forceps in the stone forward and backward, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; if the urine comes, then press your hand on what remains of the stone which is in the bladder. If it is broken, and urine spurts out, and the patient is in pain;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you cannot do this for any reason, take hold of the bone at its upper and lower extremities, then place the thumb between the two tendons, and grasp firmly; then extract the foreign body, loosen the tendon, and solidify the blood that is in the wound; and cure until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	If you cannot do this for any reason, take hold of the bone at its upper and lower extremities, then place the thumb between the two tendons, and grasp firmly; then extract the foreign body, loosen the tendon, and solidify the blood that is in the wound; and cure until it is healed.
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	When the bone is loosened in a woman, and if it does not happen again, it is a grievous cure and is defended by two things: the first is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows how to uncover her breasts as well as she does.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third method is that if by chance one cannot find a woman who is very skilled in this art of hands; and the fourth method is that if the woman’s thumb is more thick than the man’s thumb, for it can make a deeper cut, and greater pain shall ensue.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	If necessary, if you must take a young maid who is well-skilled, and prick her thumb with the needle, and if you do not find one, no matter how baseborn she may be; and present to her a woman who is wise in life, or a woman who knows how to do a part of the art, and command her to do what you command of her with inquiry of the thumb.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and look well if the woman is a maid; for you must push her head or foundation and inquire of the thumb; and if she finds it, if you constrain her foot, recommand her to hold her foot or with the patient, and press her left hand on the bladder form
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If it is true, when you move the bowels from the belly towards the groin as far as the root of the thigh; then press upon the hip in the root of the thigh and find the middle of the bone there where it is usually hidden, and feel the hip in that part; and do not move the thigh above the hip or below, and let the size be small at first.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	Then loosen the hip in the size; if you feel the hip is too large for the wound until the hip can rest firmly, and the veins that many times twist in the hips are: that is to say, small and large, twisted and blunt, long and round, and which have rings. If the veins resemble these, it is an indication of displacement.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if it does not go away, if you put in place a soaked sponge, and hold it for an hour until it is stained; then return to your work, until the hip is firm, and have the instruments that I told you about in the extraction of the hip as a home for you to help in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	If it does not go away, and it is an artery that is cut, put powder on the wound and strain with needles and thread, and do not start it again; leave the bone alone and do not move it, but by chance it dies the patient will die; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the bleeding has ceased and the limb is restored, if you return to work while the bone is still stiff, as long as the bone is firm.</start_of_turn>
de hernie carnouse	of hernia of the intestines
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing else but an assembly of moisture or white fat, which is as soft as the seeds of coriander, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac", and never is it properly in the belly of the egg if we take care that this is not the case; and it is the skin of the seed between the white fat that we have said.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this moisture is from weakness that comes from the seeds, and it is spread through that material.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And never does it come from percussion on the seeds, and this moisture has many colors: sometimes it is pale yellow, or it is without red, or black, or pale blue, and this is more;
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And these are the signs of a dislocation of this assembly, for if it is white or soft as we have said, if the abscess is round like the head of a sausage and does not yield easily, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the flesh itself, if the abscess is round with a piece of bone, and because of this it is thought that it is another sausage;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if the moisture is between the skin of the limb and the flesh, if you see it well; then when you see the color of the moisture, if it extends throughout the entire circumference, as we have said before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, therefore, that which follows the introductor, judge of that which is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we bind them with iron, if it be known that the patient is healthy according to his poverty and the swelling of his body; then we bind him on his back, on something rather high, and put a cloth over his face;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then we sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right side, and stretch out his arm to one of his ribs near the breastbone;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the spatula and cut the skin of the ribs among the ribs as far as the nipple, and be sure to make the incision straight by dividing the skin of the ribs up to the white line, and burn it superficially as much as possible;
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the spleen with a needle, about the size of a large wormhole; drain all the blood, and then put on your gloves; extend the spleen upwards; do not touch the spleen's bones, but only the spleen itself; carefully remove everything surrounding the spleen, or if you do not remove it skillfully, the blood will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the spleen suddenly bursts open during the work, if you leave it in its place when you have finished the work on the spleen; then join together the two bones of the shoulder blade at a suture, then stitch it up like the other wounds, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the spleen corrupted by another disease, if you must tie up the blood vessels that are suspended, doubting the decay of blood; then remove the bone at its entirety, drain the spleen, and stitch it up as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if the swelling is collected in three parts together, its roots are two in number; if you press the other part as you did the first equally, then wipe away the blood, and put in the wound clean linen soaked in rose oil.

et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And never is this cautery branch useful in the place of a steel needle, for it must be taken with a cultellaire cautery blade and cut through the leather of the joint; and if it be eschaufed as we have said, so that the white substance which contains the poison is discovered.

de l’aposteme des coions	from the abscess of the joints
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	The wounds that are in this section of the twig have fear in many places, for I seem to think that they are worth leaving alone.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	And I shall tell you about the work and the appearance of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that most abscesses come from wounds or sores, and sometimes from boils; and it is by experience.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is known by excessive and watery swelling, which is spread over wounds, or by percussion;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	And it is the color of the abscess according to the color of the corn; and there is no pain, and it is a grief.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And by chance an abscess is grieved with fear and pain, of dark color, and never comes from a vein or swelling of a vein.</start_of_turn>
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is not from a vein, if it is known by the position of the abscess cut, when you press it with your hand.</start_of_turn
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and you must not touch it.</start_of_turn>
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	He who is made of swelling of a vein is known by his disposition to the expression of touch of the thumbs.
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and can well make the size on this semblance, and on the other parts;

et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If it is high up on the socket, or in the blood vessels, if you must deliver all that is taut, and round off the edges.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	If the cartilage comes loose from its root or behind, if you must clamp it all, and withdraw the yolk, as we have said.</start_of_turn>

When your work is done, if you are using a woolly bandage soaked in rose oil and wine, then treat with other remedies until they are healed.</start_of_turn>
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles.
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is a wound enclosed by a covering resembling a berry, with softening of the bones.
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	and the patient groans in pain when he moves it.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and the treatment of this ailment is very dangerous like this one before mentioned,
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and all that we have said about this matter, according to what the ancients have done.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	It is necessary that you make the patient sit in a relaxed position, with the head and shoulders slightly elevated, and then support the suspension of the collarbones under your arms.

puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then I grasp firmly in the middle directly, according to the length of the limb, and I remove the corrupted moisture.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	Then I treat the wound as with others or I apply a bandage, if neither of these cause the bleeding of either of the wounds;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for in this way there is no harm, and if all the blood vessels come into view, if necessary, we can remove the wound from all the blood vessels.

de la routure dou syfac	from the root to the surface
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The event of this branch is by the section that comes or passes over the belly in the part of the flanks, because the intestines descend from that route to one of the buttocks;
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	These are four ways in which to break the jaw: by percussion, by jumping, by pressure, or by the elevation of grief of the lower lip; and in many other ways.
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	And the signs that it is from an extension of the jaw are that if there is pain and pain in the teeth, in the long tension, and does not come immediately;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	And the abscesses are equal in size up to the root, because the jaw presses on the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when the jaw is fractured, that it causes sudden pain at the start, and the abscesses are diverse in appearance, such as bursting skin and exposed bone, because of the escape of the intestine and the hardness of the jaw.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never should the limb be moved with the intestine, and is retained when it is held, and causes great pain to the patient, even when it is pressed
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments with fire there is fear, for it is known to escape.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And if the physician or patient orders that the intestines be retracted into the hand at the depth of the wound, if they can be returned there

puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	Then take a needle or if there is one, thick thread made of thirty threads, and pass it through the back part of the fat, which is behind the skin of the buttocks; after that measure, then cut the ends of the thread that appear from the needle, until there are three threads left;

de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	from the softening of the skin of the armpits.
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the armpits is softened in sick people, because the fat that is inside is softened, and is seen; and it is necessary, when we see it cured, to make the patient sit up on his back, and to stretch the softened skin over the natural skin; then to join the two layers together with a suture, and if you see, close the superfluous softened skin at two or three sutures firmly; then close between the sutures, and cure like the others wounds, until it is healed, and cut the thread.</start_of_turn>
dou chastrement	of great suffering.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Hairs that are scorched with fire are commanded to the patient to leave them long and even; and if they prick at their root, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
des hermofrodites	Hairs that are scorched with fire are commanded to the patient to leave them long and even; and if they prick at their root, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermofrodie est selonc deux manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les deux coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et deux coions. de la tentigene	Hermaphroditism is in two ways like that of women: one if between the two testicles appears as in the nature of a woman, or if there is hair, and sometimes in the urine.  And the other way if it is in women, and has on the navel like a beard and two testicles.  And the cure for the shame and the fame if it is that you cut off the testicles altogether, and the cure is like other wounds; in the second way, of those homes whose urine spurts through the skin of the testicles, if there is no cure.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tentigene is a swelling above the natural part, as long as it is too heavy to see; and many women have it as much as a hand.  This is the cure. It is necessary to hold the excess of the swelling at your hand or armpit, and to press it lightly; and do not move too much, for bleeding will not come, then the cure will be like any other cure as long as it is healthy; and there is another disease that comes from the root of the maw, and the spleen, and by chance spurts out, and is like the semblance of a knot, and for this reason it is called the ancient “madness of the womb”. If you can cut it out, as we have said concerning the tenticle, and cure it as long as it is healthy.
de erratique	De erratique.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	When something is out of its usual or proper place.
des emorroides	From hemorrhoids.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Emorroids are openings of veins which without restraint usually occur; and when they are old, they become thickened. We have already mentioned in the division the signs and symptoms; and I will say here those which resolve the cure. I say that emorroids and thick blood, when they are mixed in the marrow, and are not perceptible to the touch, if not treated with iron. Those which are at the edge of the marrow, we can perceive, are those which we can cure. It is therefore necessary that you place the woman in a cold house, then extend the ankle and grasp the heel, then sprinkle on medicinal astringents such as acacia and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then remove the pieces an hour later, and put them in cold water; and if there is any bleeding, if you make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and saffron and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and assails, and make one plaster on her back. And if it is fainting, that is good. If this does not happen, if there is still bleeding at the edge, make a wound there with a needle; then take lint and moisten it in the juice of plantain or in the juice of elderberry with wine vinegar, and make the wound bleed. And when the wound has healed, if the bleeding has ceased, that which is called ‘albathir’ is red, and is similar to a rough chief, if you cover it as I have said the thickened blood; and then the bleeding will cease.
des apostemes de la marris	Emoroids are openings of veins which without restraint usually occur; and when they are old, they become thickened. We have already mentioned in the division the signs and symptoms; and I will say here those which resolve the cure. I say that emorroids and thick blood, when they are mixed in the marrow, and are not perceptible to the touch, if not treated with iron. Those which are at the edge of the marrow, we can perceive, are those which we can cure. It is therefore necessary that you place the woman in a cold house, then extend the ankle and grasp the heel, then sprinkle on medicinal astringents such as acacia and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then remove the pieces an hour later, and put them in cold water; and if there is any bleeding, if you make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and saffron and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and assails, and make one plaster on her back. And if it is fainting, that is good. If this does not happen, if there is still bleeding at the edge, make a wound there with a needle; then take lint and moisten it in the juice of plantain or in the juice of elderberry with wine vinegar, and make the wound bleed. And when the wound has healed, if the bleeding has ceased, that which is called ‘albathir’ is red, and is similar to a rough chief, if you cover it as I have said the thickened blood; and then the bleeding will cease. And when the wound has healed, if the bleeding has ceased, that which is called ‘albathir’ is red, and is similar to a rough chief, if you cover it as I have said the thickened blood; and then the bleeding will cease.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Emorroids are openings of veins which without restraint usually occur; and when they are old, they become thickened. We have already mentioned in the division the signs and symptoms; and I will say here those which resolve the cure. I say that emorroids and thick blood, when they are mixed in the marrow, and are not perceptible to the touch, if not treated with iron. Those which are at the edge of the marrow, we can perceive, are those which we can cure. de l’enfantement	From infancy.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	From infancy. A master first learns at play what is the natural figure of infancy, and the signs are when you see the woman press her belly and desire to smell the breast: then the child immediately sucks; and when the child’s limbs are in accordance with the natural figure, and his head comes out first, and the second comes with him; and when you see these signs, if you gently press his belly, if the child sucks, that is enough; for when he descends on his head, if the second comes with him, and the mother is contented with his superabundances by his good upbringing; this is not natural. For it never comes from his toes, but from the womb or the hips, or the hands, or from his belly, or from behind, and is caused by some chance or other evil figure; if the master is learned in play to be wise and discreet in these things, and is wary of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures in which you must help him.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	When the child comes out of his head naturally, and the woman gives birth and her strength is weak, if you make her sit on a chair, or the women hold her; and she gives birth of oil or fennel or whatever is pleasing, and then you must hold the child between her two legs, which is his natural shape:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And split the second finger, and bind its nail until the moisture that is in its core comes out; and press the woman’s belly until the fetus descends, and if it does not descend, if you must, clench the woman with muscle spasm of ruegra with oil of sesame; then make her take and expel menstrual blood, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: if the fetus is now expelled. And if the two hands go out forcefully, if you must, hold them lightly together and together; and if they will not enter, if put the woman on the seat, and hold her feet high; then pull the seat out of the ground, and hold her, that she does not move during the pulling; and if the hands do not enter, and the fetus dies, if you grip the hands at the wrist that was put before, and pull out the child, and comfort her equally.

de l’issue des gemelz	When the dislocation is slight

When there is a fracture of the bone, it often happens that the blood vessels are ruptured, and sometimes the bone is split in two or even three places; and this is not a strange thing, and often happens.

de l’enfant mort	From childhood death.
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat a woman in childbirth who has lost her child, or her womb, as I have said in the previous chapter, and there is no imminent danger, you are constrained by the work of your hands

Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	And after that comes the form of pressure, which we find in the books; and to-day there are two tears of blood from two veins.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the horns should be more subtle than restrictive, and should be made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	And let the mouth be open wide, that is to say two fingers wide, and the jaw wide, and long one palm and a half.
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	And in between let the two lips be two thumbs wide open, which are closed one against the other, half a palm or more long.</start_of_turn>
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	And these two positions are held in the mouth of the patient for opening when one turns the two corners.</start_of_turn>
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, more subtle and lighter, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the shape of the nails;
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	And thus he has twice as many joints as fists, as you see, of a palm long and two broad.
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	And when you see the matrix open with all the instruments, if you make the woman sit with one leg lit, the pieces steady and the legs outstretched,
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then take the two fists together in the matrix, and hold the chief of the instrument between her thighs;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then open the mouth of the matrix with all the instruments, if you have made the tension equal, according to the quantity that you see open the matrix, until it boils like it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all very burdensome, and their resemblance is multiplied; and when one sees them appear, one is more hasty in their work and more anxious about the quantity of them.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If one does not despair of the instrument when it does not appear, for its necessity is not easily excused
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the second is retained in infancy, if you command the patient that she should retain her limb, and then make her expel it with difficulty, and hold your hands to her mouth and nose;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she leaps for this, well is that.
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If not, take one pot and make a hole or incision, and put herbs in it that can open the mouth of the marrow, like camomile, rue, anis, chamomile, cassia and centaury.
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	All these herbs, or some of them, should be boiled in water over the fire; then put a scab or incision in the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the marrow.
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	and leave it until steam comes from the marrow; then make it spit out, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second joint is seized with pain.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if it remains after this treatment, and is not forced out, as is commanded in the dance, let her moisten her left hand with oil of sesame or in almond paste, and then hold it in its natural position.</start_of_turn>
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and then grasp the second; and when she has found it, if she grasps it and extends it forward and backward, so that the hand does not bleed during the extraction.</start_of_turn
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but must move slightly to the side and back, and then treat her; for it will come out and dry up.</start_of_turn>
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the marrow is open, as we have said, for the cure of yesterday, and fumigation of herbs.
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it is not from all that we have said, if you keep that you do not use to your treatment;
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the marrow, you bind to the hip of the woman, and then clench with ointment tetrafarmaçon;
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	if the marrow breaks and comes out, and comes out with force; however, when it breaks in this way, if there comes a bad smell from the stomach and the head, and it makes the patient vomit.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it be necessary, then fumigations are useful in this case: neither of the ancients have proved the efficacy of fumigation with fennel and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument in which we fumigate the woman is to retain the flowers and secondine if it is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is to be seen like a cane, and put the head in the middle, and the large heads on the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and either the fumigations over the charcoal, and the pitch until it is consumed, and start another.
de percier lou fondement	From the root to the ground.
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	None are born who do not have the root firmly grasped, for it is grasped by an subtle sap.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	then you must compel her to dance so that she breaks that sap at its root, and do not prick her with a sharp object, and keep the pressure so that she does not touch it;
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a wet cloth in wine and oil, and then cauterize until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	If you doubt that it will stay in place, put or draw a weight on it, and hold the hands still, and let the limb rest until the pain subsides.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	Under no circumstances must you stop treatment for wounds or abscesses; if you do cover the treatment: if either is cured, as we have said concerning the weight.
de la fistule dou fondement	of fistula from its foundation.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from the foundation are nodular, and those that come from below the foundation are more forceful, or in the space of the two parts,
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	If there is a fistula or several of them; and when that swelling is ancient, if it has been there for a long time, and is accompanied by moisture which oozes white bile or soft pus,
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	These fistulas never remain permanent; they are known by the fact that they discharge or evacuate, or cause vomiting whenever the patient evacuates, and sometimes by chance they break through.</start_of_turn>
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	If there are fistulas which break through to the bladder, and half way up the thigh; and reach as far as the joint of the hip, and even to the knee.</start_of_turn>
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows the permanent fistula from the temporary one.
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And it is that you bite down your thumb or foundation, and insert a subtle needle of spider or iron into the fistula when there is no distortion.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is distortion, if you insert a slight attempt, or hair of a horse, as long as you feel the attempt or the hair on your thumb;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and there is neither bleeding nor wind nor swelling, as we have said.
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	The liquid that comes out should not pierce the skin; if you are in a hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula persists up to the bladder or the urinary tract, if in a leap the urine escapes, and cannot be retained by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is perceived up to the hip joint, if it is the vein that is leaking up to the limb;
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no swelling and the pain is not severe, if it is only slight, and no medicine or ointment will suffice
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these persistent fistulas there is no other cure than toil, and the folly of the fools who interfere with it.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In that which is neither new nor old, hope for health by fire, as I have seen.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	And that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and that you support the legs up to his thighs, and that you incline his thighs towards his belly.
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	Then make an attempt to join the shoulder, or if there is stiffness, until you can see or feel that it is coming together.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels pain at the base, if you must, bite down on your thumb and index finger,
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	You sense that it has already been perceived; and whether it is revealed or you sense between your shoulder and your ear the jaw or the head, then the liquid that is present is spit out.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if it does not slip away by itself, it cannot be healed.</start_of_turn>
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	We can do everything well enough to heal it, but this is not enough.</start_of_turn
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and if we do it like this, if it is small, we will cauterize it as it should be; if it is large, we will do it with a larger cautery.</start_of_turn
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	And the whole limb hangs out through the fistula, as far as it comes from the foundation; make this once or twice, until you know that these worms that are like a hair of an eel must be burned, which are similar to a nail.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	Then the healer of soft swellings embeds them with burning, until those worms are forced out; then he heals the wound stitching together the hair and skin.</start_of_turn>
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If he is still sane, that is good. But if not, he will not be sane;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur.
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	and if it attempts between, and does not pierce until it reaches the root which is or underlies, and between your thumb and the attempt put on a thick covering of hair or wool, and you will see the fistula at the place where it underlies the covering of hair.
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and will be delivered the attempt, and cured; then bind those hairs that seem like a hen’s quill, and nothing remains of them
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if he does not move from you, and stands between you and the work, if you cauterize with fire or medicine at its peak.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For indeed, the cautery of fire brings together these two bones, namely, the burning of these bones together, the bursting of blood and the drying of moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	Then the cure of soft tissues, boiled or crushed in broth, until it boils over, and is forced out by the burning of the bones in the broth;
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Then cure the wound of the suppuration of soft parts with strong charcoal, and the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, if it is sound and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes up to the root of the bone, and is pushed out of place, if its bone or root is fractured, inquire about that.</start_of_turn>
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel a tremor, and between these lies the thread or the sinew or the bone, or it is about to pierce, if there is no other way out but by opening up and hoping, by the administration of one of these three methods:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you bind it until it is healed, or if you dare, you take it out if you put in attempts and cure it as before.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	And do not linger too long, for you must cover the dwelling that holds the foundation, and come out with the egestions in the desired direction.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	Then withdraw it, as we have said;
