Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And never are fistulas like this: and it is when you bite the attempt in the fistula, and it is either at the cost of the skin above the wound, or at the cost of the lower part of the foundation.
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	if you take a perceived attempt at the head like this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And there is always a thread torn in two, and you must hold the attempt at the very end of the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If the person is in the margin of the jawbone downwards, then draw out the thread of that which is pierced, so that you swallow your tooth or jawbone.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	Draw out the head of the thread and reunite the teeth together, and strain one against the other, and leave it hanging there for a while or two.</start_of_turn>
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	And do not restrain it at any time, until the thread has caught these hairs which are between two teeth, and that they are biting;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	Then cure the wound until it is healed and healthy.</start_of_turn>
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not perforate, if you force it to perforate in every way you can, it will not be too much harm.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not proper to make the wound wider by force, and then to cure it, as we have said, while it is still healthy.</start_of_turn>
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The form of the thorny bladder from which the fistula is made is rough and torn at one end and trenchant;
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on must not cope with it, as you can see here.</start_of_turn
des emorroydes	Des emorroydes.
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Swelling of the veins occurs in two ways: either they are filled with blood to the point of being like small grains of resin, or there are both large and small blood clots inside them, and this causes pain and bleeding.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and there may be one or more of them, and they are driven out of the foundation and the head of the bone; but those which are driven out are accompanied by moisture.
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and are accompanied by either blood clots or a yellow fluid or blood, and have a yellow color.
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	And the cure for these things that are within the foundation, if you command the patient to sigh to leave the room, as long as the foundation is firm, and it appears; then they will go away.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	If you hurry, and you hold it with your nails, or you hold it at your finger, then you must break it at its roots
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if it is united [with other bones] they will not hold by their moisture; if you take hold of them with cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamlet.
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and you pull them from your shoulders, then you break them, and dust off the above-mentioned warm powders which are in place of cautery.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	Or thou cauterisest them as it is said or as the treatise of cautery teaches thee, and then thou curest them of other cures so long as they be sound.
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	And if the foundations cannot endure, if thou clenchest the patient’s jaw firmly and graspest firmly what is or underlies, so that it can openly issue forth;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	The patient cannot bear the pain, and if the thread is too strong for the foundation, the cure is slight;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	And that thou grasp them at thy nail or hold them, and break them, then cure them as we have said, so long as they be sound, and that thou fear not the incision with the knife.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	If you command that I restore the shoulder according to this manner: take one thread and pierce it through a needle, then pass the thread through below and draw the needle out from the other side, and twist the two threads at the base of the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	If there is much looseness; hold the thread taut, then knot the thread and pull out the needle, and make sure all the others are tight, and leave one to correct the excess blood;
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then place upon the foundation one moist bandage in rose oil or beeswax, and place upon the foundation, and command the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then leave it as long as it hurts, and when it softens, if the treatment for swelling and other treatments, while it is still sane.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	When the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	Then the physician must treat it until it is healed if it is necessary;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot be calmed, if he must renew the scraping more forcefully than before, until it comes out, and be escorted.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the physician must treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	When the physician hears the patient groaning.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Formice is a small outgrowth that appears before the limb, and goes out from behind the body.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	It never touches the bone, and is felt as if dead weight, and comes over the entire limb, more than at any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a needle of goose feather or a strong needle of bull, and put that needle on the wound, until it turns blue around the wound all around
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Then turn your hand to the whole extent of the needle until you reach all around the wound, and put it out from behind, and press the wound from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	If you see that he does it with a spider's thread or iron in this fashion, be subtle and withdraw your hand.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	If you see that he does it with a spider's thread or iron in this fashion, be subtle and withdraw your hand, for it must hold firmly and press.  If you see that he does it with the fire cautery, if it is before or alongside the cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of this fashion.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never make a blister of silver or gold, or of spiders’ thread melted or twisted; and never make of these instruments small or large, as they are presented.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who are feeble and painful in the treatment of children are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	Their form is small and great if it is excessive; or the belly is bound up in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and there is a swelling or the belly is bound up, as you see, and the limb is pierced either from the front or from behind; and there is a wound at one of the ribs, or in the other at the hip bone.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and either the belly or one puts the medicines in a bladder of gut or parchment, and either pierce all around the wound,
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	And there is between each hole [in the burn] one must leave space, then go into these holes one strong thread of strong thread twisted into a cross or hooked; and assemble the belly like a nail.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And when the medicine is inside, if the thread has in front of it a strong thread, then clip; and that is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine neither be too hot nor too cold, and join the head of the clip with oil or balm of egg, or something similar, and then tighten it lightly;
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	Then hold the patient’s hands together, until it is all visible, then remove the clip, and let the patient rest his legs at leisure.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And if the physician sees that the patient is feverish, if the bite is severe as much as possible; and if he sleeps all night through, it is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see him lying in sickness with a swelling of the belly, and the physician hastens to leave, if he resumes as soon as he is well.</start_of_turn>
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if there is swelling in the marrow or foundation, or abscess, if either be as subtle as with a child;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and that is the shape of a subtle blister on which the skin is strained:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in this chapter the treatment of wounds; or you may call it the treatment of hands and medicine, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse depending on what causes them, and depending on the limbs or wounds that are made, and how they are made
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things that cause wounds are by the bite of a stone, and the size of a nail or a nail, or of a lance or a fist or a knife, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	Or that which is made according to the laws of custom, if like a wound that occurs upon the neck, or the head, or the arm, or the belly, or the liver, or other limbs.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	Or that which is made according to the laws of custom, if like a wound that occurs upon the neck, or the head, or the arm, or the belly, or the liver, or other limbs. And I shall tell you of the cure for simple wounds, and I shall begin with wounds of the head alone, for the memory will return to this chapter.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes or a head wound, and the bone is not broken, if you take care that there is no cracking of bone or other things, and the skin is entirely torn and the wound is great,  </start_of_turn
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	And you doubt the wound excessively: if you do it too often, it will make the head of the sufferer even sicker, even though blood comes from the wound itself; or the blood comes from the opposite side of the wound.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and listen carefully to the patient’s complaints of wine and meat that are spoiled
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	and if he does not see an improvement, if either he has aversion to meat or does not drink wine, does not eat bread;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put out the wound, if an abscess comes, cover it with soft cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in astringent wine;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	If there is no surrounding tissue around the wound, put it on the wound while it is still fresh with all its blood; and it will not be moved by air, dust, or anything else.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it has already moved, put on some ointment, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is great like the size of a spear and similar, and the limbs do not naturally unite, if you unite them with sutures, as I will say, for wounds of the belly, with sutures.</start_of_turn
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is uncovered from bone, and is raw, and will hold only with a little pressure; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hair instead of skin,
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And command the patient to eat coarse meats, such as testicles and wheat germ, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find or smell decay, and it is not at the bone, if you pierce it completely, and drain the pus, then cure it.</start_of_turn>
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which without cure, and it cannot be held by medicines, if you must cauterize it, and if you find it dislocated, if you bind it with a thread.</start_of_turn
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if this does not help, if you must cauterize.</start_of_turn
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, if it is a slight cure: put on this powder that solidifies just as well as it was moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; and chalk three parts, and mix the powder thoroughly.</start_of_turn>
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply the wound, and bind it firmly, until it heals well and rejoins all its substance.</start_of_turn
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bind it firmly, and let it loosen, if it does not swell; for we do not stay the medicine until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never shall one do this treatment alone, when there is neither incense nor blood of a dragon, but only when the wound has not moved.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the wound has moved, even in this case, if one does not put in this powder;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some digestive unguents or poultices made of barley flour and water and honey, until it boils over;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if a fracture of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, if you extract the foreign body cautiously;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And I will tell you later about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If there is no difference between the fracture of the head and the fracture of the neck, but if the neck or the artery is cut
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If this is the source of the pain, if there is nothing else to do but leave the wound open, do not put anything restrictive, for it is night and they shrink back;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	Do not put any ointment on the wound, for the substance of the wound is cold, and its continuation is with the marrow, which is the most solid part of the limb.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but if there is some medicine, such as warm bath in sweet water, mixed with rose oil, and barley bathed in sweet water,
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other stones of mine according to this manner, and moist patches.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, if the blood vessel and the nerves are torn, then cure as long as it is healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wound is deep and blood vessels are torn and filled with blood, if the opening is high or low down there;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	If the artery is severed, blood flows out, if the dressing and cautery are not properly applied together.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	If the spine of the jaw is fractured, or the cheekbone, and the bone is fractured, by which the meat will go forward,
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	If the thumb is stiff on the wrist of the throat, and do not touch the throat but rather return it to its natural position.
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then strain will follow immediately, and leave it alone for a while, then treat with ointments until it is healed;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	If the wound has made an indentation in the bone, if necessary;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are bone fragments, if the broken pieces are too numerous to count, and if you cannot count them, leave them until the wound has healed,
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	Or let it be loosened and aligned the issue.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wound is fresh, if powder over powder as I have said.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is fistula, if the wound must be closed as I have said in this chapter.</start_of_turn>
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of a wound from a lance or a knife.</start_of_turn
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it be a wound from a lance or a dagger, and the wound be deep, if thou seest that the wound has burst open violently, the patient's life hangs in the balance; for the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	If it be not deep and is fresh throughout its extent, if thou seest that it be not clotted at the first hour with powder, do not tie it up with the blood lest thou do more harm than good.</start_of_turn>
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	Go back to the body and comfort the patient.</start_of_turn>
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	But I put an attractive weight on it, and I hold it together for the third time.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you do not have a weight, put in the wound much cotton to suck out the moisture.
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and let the patient rest on the wound for two or three days, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there is no spasm, do not tremble badly or move excessively
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	When you see bones displaced, if the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	When you see bones displaced, if the wound is saved, cure the wound and other cures as long as they are healthy;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot be healed, and if there is an opening, as there is fistula; if the cure is like that which must be done.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is an incision of a spear or knife, and it is simple or deep, or at the back, if the cure of what is before;
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	If it is large, of suture; if it is small, of powder, and if it is pressed into the bone, and has broken pieces, if the wound is gaping and the veins are bursting if they are severed.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	If they are not severed, if it leaves the wound open, if it aligns the extractions;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and other wounds as other members is the judgment if as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	indeed
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The pain of the belly is great and strong and slight.
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	There is great pain from a great wound never leaving the intestines, or the nerves of the intestines, because of the admission of pus
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the swelling is more painful, and never is less harmful than a small wound than a great one,
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	because of this the veins are more heated and more thick than the blood;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	Forasmuch the intestines swell greatly that they feel the fruit, if they return more inwards,
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	Therefore, when the intestines swell greatly that they feel the fruit, if they return inwards, the belly is often painful, so we must keep the intestines in their place as well as other things.</start_of_turn>
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And such is the way of vomiting from the belly three times: </start_of_turn
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the three common costures come in the cost of the belly.</start_of_turn
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	And the stitching of other wounds with thorns and three others is common as other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	And all of them are more pure with the stitching of the belly, and I shall say one thing and declare.</start_of_turn>
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small and nothing of the intestines is pressing,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and anything is to be held in, that is by one of the two methods:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	Or for the smallness of the wound, as we have said.
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	Or because the intestines are swollen with fruit.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, swallow slowly in a small quantity:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	wet a sponge or take a small piece of cloth dipped in lukewarm water only,

et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and never does this wine restrain, and is mute that awe soul because of swelling.

car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	For in this matter, the entrance to many things is aligned;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, if one makes an opening at the instrument of coping, the swellings are held together.</start_of_turn>
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is immobile as the size,
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	for it is not necessary to cut too deeply.</start_of_turn>
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	And this is the instrument for cutting.
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if the trench is made downwards in the curve and does not burst forth, and once this is done:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	and when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines are pulled out,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	if you reset it according to its natural form in its own place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	If you are in doubt, for this is worth knowing.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is large and is in the lower part of the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	you must know that you must manage the patient behind his back

et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and if it is in the lower part of the belly, and if the root of the belly is in either of the two lower parts.

et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And so it is proper to administer that which I have said concerning great and oozing wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	Small wounds leave that which has appeared,
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then hold between your hands.i. administer with pity all the way through,
et assemble les levres;	and assemble the limbs;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	And this is the common method of stitching.
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and take a needle or several, according to the amount of the wound's size,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave some space from the wound edge. i.e. to do an interval, and pierce a needle or there is much strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and make a knot at the end of the thread.
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	Who is soaked with the leather inwards, as long as you make it pierce from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	Who is soaked with the leather inwards, as long as you make it pierce from that part, and gather the chief from the sip of the three together.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then the strain of a double thread is put around the needle of three parts,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then gather the three parts of the wound evenly,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	Then leave a space between the teeth and insert another hook.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then keep the thread taut as when you did the first hook,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not stop doing this until you have made several hooks,
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until all the wound is secured;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	And be the nails blunt, between soft and hard,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	for the blunt nails grasp all the hair, and the too hard if they do not penetrate well.</start_of_turn>
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore it is recommended that they be blunt.</start_of_turn>
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and must not push the nails too far from the hair and skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	They do not hold and open the wound before the suture.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then hold the head of the arrow, so that it does not wound the patient while sleeping.
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I put bands or dressings on the head of the arrow to hold it,
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and I leave them until the wound is closed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	And this method of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds.
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because there is a needle or two involved.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is easier to make.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	And when you have recognized these things all together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	if you keep the hook at the part or where you have begun, in the manner in which it would cost the guts.</start_of_turn>
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put between every stitch the thickness of a little finger;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitch will hold the flesh,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	And I closed a wound there where one had a wound or an abscess,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	which was caused by a cut.</start_of_turn>
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and it was more than a palm wide.</start_of_turn
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and there was blood coming out of it for more than two palms' length.</start_of_turn
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	And there was the wound in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	And I brought back the intestines when they had been out for twenty-three hours.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	And the wound was closed after fifteen days, and the patient recovered, and was healed
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the people saw that he was going to die, and this was a miracle.
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	And I will not linger any longer, for I am in one place where there is no coming or going, no medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And thus I must depart more than once upon a wound, and I give it a drink of honey until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Or thus you will say the two proper ways of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and pass it from the underside of the part furthest from the edge up to this very one;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	When she has perceived the right knee to the right, if the head of the shoulder is sucked in, twisted or you have pulled out the awl,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and makes her perceive from the other side from the inside until it escapes.</start_of_turn>
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and you understand this matter as well as a leatherworker does the leather.</start_of_turn>
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and that you leave one part of the shoulder free, and then take hold of it again, until the dislocation is completely over.</start_of_turn>
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second method of stitching, which Galiens does so discreetly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	if it is as if no one does it, who assemble the parts naturally.
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and join one of the bosses to the other boss, in a part like this:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	insert a needle or chief of silk nearby, and make the one that is only pierced bleed.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	et laisse les poils dou syfac.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then prick at their base, and hold the eyes steady until they grow to this extent.
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as the hairs grow long and even;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then prick at their base, and hold the eyes steady until they grow to this extent, like other hairs on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	And this is the most common and trifling way of stitching.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	So be it that this word is false, and no one testifies to it.</start_of_turn>
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	we must sew the belly with two needles, or there should be thread in the hem.</start_of_turn
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and we must push one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew corroises;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	And towels that when they are returned into the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	And towels that when they are returned into the belly, if the stitching is more tight than usual inside the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judge of the wound shall be like the judge of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, even though it has moved,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	If he returns to stop the intestine, and look out; then put on the powder that prevents char,
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	If he has moved it [the intestine], if look out; then put on no covering whatever is there, until the wound has healed.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and bind the thread, and be careful the blood does not clot, and look after him.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure the wound like the others, until it is healed;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	And if you have no medicines, if you put it on, as soon as it begins to swell, cotton wool,
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	And if you have no medicines, if you put it on, as soon as it begins to swell, cotton wool, and move it just once the joint is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For in many cases the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	if you doubt that the wound will not heal properly, leave the principal limb alone,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	If it seems good to you, moisten a clean cloth with hot linseed oil or rosemary oil.
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	And put it over the wound, and soak the area with it;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	if there is pain or putrefaction in the belly, and it often happens,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	if the black vomit of wine makes you dizzy, and the putrefaction comes right up to the intestines;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	And the spleen, and the intestines which when they are large are lighter to heal than the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The large intestines cannot be healed when they are swollen
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	because of the distension of the veins, and by the subtlety of the whole body, and by the proximity of its nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	and if the wound bursts, if it is reset backwards just as the intestine, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	If it is black and becomes either white or black, know that you must bind the black limb, that blood does not flow from it.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	and then close what is between the bones,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the joints apart from the sore part until the bone is straightened, and the wound is bowed.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the root of the boil.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is round and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	if the belly is restored in a gentle manner,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I know that one has fallen from a horn or the belly of a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	And it was the wound at the side of the stomach.
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	And it was filled and became a fistula, and in this it was vomiting and diarrhea.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I put in cure accordingly, and did not cease until it was healed, and the wound closed
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it closed, I doubted that the patient would be well in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	And there is no harm, but it delays for many arrangements, meals and drinks.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	And they say that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be ligated in a timely manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	immediately take great care, and then gather the layers of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the fremis has opened the mouth, if it is on the two layers,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	If she stretches her mouth above;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	then she holds her head still, and this remains as long as she cannot loosen it.
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then she puts another remedy afterwards in the same way as before, until the wound is fully healed;
et cout la plaie.	and closes the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	If the head of the shoulder burns in the intestine, and causes no harm to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and one can tie the intestine with a fine thread which is cut from the intestine of a beast.
en teil maniere:	in this way.
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the head of this thread of intestine that is well cut through,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	Then he seizes the head of the thread, namely a fine thread of linen twisted.
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Then he threads the needle and sews the gut, and holds it in place in the groove;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this way of stitching does not go beyond the way of the vein and the hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, even if it is in one of the great intestines, if there is no other remedy, except for slightness.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	Of fistula or that it be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Of fistula or that it be, any wound or incision, when it breaks open, is universally called a fistula.
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and even when it is closed and bound together.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	and fistula is truly a wound that must be closed firmly and cleanly, or one does not feel pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And it is also like the quill of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	never in a clean jump, and sometimes widely spread.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	never too much, and sometimes enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and as I have already said concerning wounds, that every wound that is not cleansed, and that has pus,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	This is not fire but by one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	namely, by the smallness of blood or bone;
ou por sa malice;	or by its wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hardness within and on the eyelids, that does not allow new hair to grow.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	Or there is too much swelling;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	Or the limb is swollen, and the matter is of poor quality.
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	Or the medicine is not good in the cure.
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	Or because the corruption is like pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	Or for the property in the region is tardy the digestion, and tardy the healing, and flees by nature.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	Or there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already mentioned these causes, the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or you must know that I will tell you the cure of fistula which is made by an egg of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Hair that has become infected fistulates in all limbs with pain.
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	because there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves.
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or at the hip, or in the intestines, or in the bladder, or in some of the bones,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or at the back of the spine, or at any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	And if a part comes to the property of the main limb, and there are similar symptoms.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are of this kind are of grievous healing, and there is nothing but toil and ignorance.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is no fistula that does not reach the root except as I have said, and you have promised a cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you shall know if it is straight, if the pain is gone;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	If the fistula is tortuous, if the hook of a subtle substance attempts to sink,
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for the swelling swells inward towards the curvature.</start_of_turn>
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has holes and you do not keep it well contained by hooks,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	if the liquid leaks through one of the holes,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	For the moistness is so strong from a part to another, and the earth is moistened.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then when its weight is suddenly taken away from its foot, you must know if there is bone or nerve, and that the limb is immersed in the wound
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you press your hand, and the limb he feels it in;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	then when you know truly the limb or it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or a vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	Or in some of the limbs that I have mentioned, if the bone follows what I have said,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	And the bone will be forced out for the swelling and corrupted marrow that is within.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then the limb must be treated until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is well deep from the right side, if you must, cope them out as well.</start_of_turn
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	Then I put soft bands in medicine, and I hold them until the head of the fistula.
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medicine consumes the excess which is dissolved at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put greasy ointments on the wound, until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it does not heal by this, if I must, I will cauterize as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, if it breaks.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If the vein or nerve is not grasped or the principal members, as we have said before.
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	And if the bone is discovered, and there is corruption and blackness, if the marrow remains as long as the corruption is entirely bony,
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then you must cure the things that are causing harm until they are healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	If he is not well, and bows low as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	if he is not well, and bows low as before,
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if he is not well, and bows low as before, keep your eyes fixed, do not move until they grow back.
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and restore the limb;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	And if it is firmly bound, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, grasp that the corruption has progressed too far, that you will not be able to do anything about it.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other remedy but to leave it to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small broken bone, and you attempt to treat it with tweezers,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if the extraction is with a suitable instrument,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is any bone left, if the teeth are broken, do not leave them in place;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if moisture opposes you, and there is no doubt or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	if bone and moisture and fire and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you do not remove them at once, if you put something over the wound that promotes putrefaction,
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and leave them as long as the bones are pierced through them.</start_of_turn>
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	so that it will cause less damage to the bones;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	it is better to leave the wound open.</start_of_turn>
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	If the blackness is so great that the corruption is as black as bone,
puis restoure la plaie;	Then restore the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a great part of corruption, and it comes up to the marrow of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if you can cover and cover all until the corruption is gone, and then cure it until it is healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	And I shall tell you of a fistula that happened in a man’s leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	if you take this as an example and assist in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	There was once a young man about .xxx. years of age, who had pain in his leg caused by something within the bone,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	so that the matter came to his leg, and there was no apparent cause for the wound;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	But the marrow above all the bones above,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and in bursting out of matter, it becomes a fistula, and there comes out pus that covers the wound and moisture from the marrow.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and remains for a year, and there is no art in the hand of man,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	as long as I recall it, and saw his limb and the medicines with which he was being cured,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	And that which is cured by the wounds acquires great strength.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	And became red the skin of the young man, and had the color of citron.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I bound a thread in one of these wounds, and then encircled all the wounds,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that one vein was found to be near the other throughout the limb.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I grasped it then, and I grasped in one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone.
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and I found it broken and I perceived it, and I could see the decay right up to the bone within;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I saw that which appeared to me of a broken bone, and I thought that there was no further decay, except for that which I had seen already.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound with healing medicines so long as I could, but I could not bind it;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	And then I repeated [the procedure], and I uncovered the bone as before.
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	And I found the corruption continuing in the bone, and the marrow, and then the bone itself, and I thought to solder the limb.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could only do so as long as I grasped a part of the bone, and the traitor forced me to do all his work,
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored the medicine; and he was healed and bound soundly again.
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	And must not be recommenced for the weakness of the patient, who is unable to bear it.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death which I avoid for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For often there is the evacuation of blood, but it was cured entirely,
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and there was left in the place of the bone a hard scale, and it was in perfect condition and caused no discomfort or hindrance of any kind, neither to the patient nor to the doctor.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is fractured in no place of pain, if you must suture it in this manner.
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take one thread, and strain at the head of the bone that breaks,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command that it does not extend further upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and make the knot closer to its place and the knot further away from its place.
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	And thus is the head [of the shoulder] displaced, so that if you pull out the corrupt flesh from its socket,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	if you uncover the bone above the joint or you see marrow, that the bone does not move from the socket.
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	put a cushion or a small board under the bone to cover the corrupt flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and so you must do until you see and feel the corruption, and do it again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	then uncover the whole limb; then place one stone weight,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then stretch from one part to the other the corruption, and hold the bone steady for as long as the corruption lasts;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, if you join the corrupted bone, and hold the bone that contains the other part;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And if the corruption is in the continuity of the two joints, if there is no other vessel except the duct;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	And if the corruption is or the bone is fractured in the hand or in the foot, if it is very strong in that matter.
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but always you must inquire concerning the corruption, how it happened to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and the wound must be kept clean in every way, but that the vein or nerve is not injured;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	And the thread which he cuts and the silk which covers these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of swellings.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their greatness and their thinness, and their magnitude and their smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason it is necessary to consider the appearance of the work of his instrument.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and the thread which he cuts and the silk which covers these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of swellings.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	And the witness to the methods of diseases.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you think the instrument with which you are dealing is appropriate according to what is commanded.</start_of_turn>
dou feu	indeed fire.
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The limb is swollen or by moisture, or by heat;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	And when you have treated that corrosion with medicines, it will be of no avail.
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	if you must cover that limb until the corrosion has passed
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	if the patient escapes by this means of death, or by malice, which is greater, the fault of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the limb becomes black, as if burned by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	And after the black bile, then comes the corrosion of member to member.
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and grasp it through all the body; if you are in a hurry, cover
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if there is percussion from venomous beasts, as with scorpions of the sea and vipers and others,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	and the marrow is lost from its life.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, if the pulp is at the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach the forearm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes up to the arm, if the pulp is at the bone, so that the corrosion does not reach the elbow; and if it passes the bone, that is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no other remedy but the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and all the more that the corrosion comes or goes: if it comes in the first joint, if the pulp follows the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	And if it comes or if it is pressed, if you can manage it, grasp all the hair.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	And if it rises in the limb, if you can manage it, grasp at the joint of the armpit
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	And if it comes from below the armpit, if there is no other remedy but to leave the patient to die;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and you must tie up the limb from below and above
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	And extend one minister from the lower limb, and another minister from the upper limb.
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	And you will loosen the flesh that is between the two limbs at a wide span, until the bone is uncovered.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then grasp or seize it, and put a bandage of lint under one part, so that the silk does not touch the sound limb,
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and come to the patient with other wound and incision.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if bleeding comes from the wound when you work, if you cauterize the limb immediately,
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or you put on some restraining powders; then return to your work until it is accompanied by something.</start_of_turn>
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the limb securely with a strong bandage, and treat it until it is healed;
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I tell you that there was once a man in our home.
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	He had a blackening that seemed to burn with fire.
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corruption first arose in his armpit, so that it blackened the whole limb.</start_of_turn>
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when we saw the corruption, if we covered the limb with cloth, it was healed.</start_of_turn
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long after the corruption returned to the arm or shoulder, and I came to you,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	And I put upon them things that rebound after the softening of the tumor, and I cannot stop its corrosion.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	And he swears that I must hold his hand, and I do not wish, for I fear to impede the matter from rebounding
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I doubt that if I cut off his hand, he will not die.
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for the man’s spirit was weak; and he arose completely, and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	And so he held his hand covered, and it healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And I have heard of this matter only because of that which we make elsewhere if necessary.</start_of_turn>
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Never comes a fistula in the marrow, and stays so long that it makes great swelling of the bone;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it bursts and breaks, and in the leap it breaks the bone, and makes the marrow burst, just like a vessel;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	And the skin which is below is as subtle as fine woven damask.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and does not reach the bone or the nerve, and such ailments are called "sain".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and is not called "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so elongated that it reaches the bone embedded in the marrow, it is called "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	And if the leather is tough, if you grasp it tightly, even when it is subtle, like a drape.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	And do not be afraid because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	If you have clasped it and the leather is soft, and the corruption is not great,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the leather is thick as a cloak, if the surgeon has the cure of clisters nearby:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	Observe if the wound is large, and the bowel that is in it smells of foulness.
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Therefore perform the Egyptian medicinal plaster which is thus made:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take alum, oil, and beeswax, equally, and mix them together in a vessel over a fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	Then take according to your need, and make it hot and sweet.
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	Then clamp the limb firmly and hold the opening;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	Leave the medicine in place for three hours, then remove it cautiously.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Do this several times, until the limbs are limp and the bones are loosened.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	And never is the abscess pierced with aqua of amber.
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and you take amber powder of must from grapes, and pour water down,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then the swelling will drain, and you will clench, until you are sure that the wound is well healed.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot endure it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the aqua of amber,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	If the cluster of acute and honey-like blisters or if there be a piece of clotted blood broiled;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you broil it with honey and wine, that the honey has the property of softening and washing away,
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the wound dry.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you have fixed that the wound is well softened,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	If the cluster of that which makes birth comes out whole in him,

ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or thou doest cauterize it with some medicines and unguents, of which I have said the properties or treat with unguents.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the opening of the wound is small, and the cluster cannot enter,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	If the edge of a wound is wide, and put on an Egyptian bandage,
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or a basic dressing, as much as it is widened;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too wide, if the nails remain too long or if the clot enters,
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	or if the tissue below breaks through to the bone, if the wound is too deep.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the limb is in fracture, if you do not leave it to mend naturally;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you do not cover its wounds as you see fit,</start_of_turn>
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	it will slip down to the lowest point.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	For when the limb is in fracture, if you do not leave it to mend naturally;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	And if you do not cover your face with your sleeve as you see,

et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	And these wounds are those which arise from the bowel, whether it be poison or wound or enough, or digested, or indigestible.

car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	And if it swells excessively after treatment, the swelling that was not there before remains; and the veins become dark and do not swell.

si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	If indeed it is a matter of dizziness, for there is a great amount of phlegm, it is the last remedy.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take an emetic to bring up the phlegm, and do so with rose oil and vinegar in equal measure by weight.</start_of_turn>
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then keep him still and quiet; and this itself makes honey easily digest.</start_of_turn
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when there is no more dizziness,

de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the boil.</start_of_turn>
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panarice is an abscess that arises from the swelling of the pouch of the hand.
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or from a bite, or by chance it arises in other places too;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	if it comes to an abscess, it must be treated immediately, if one does not take precautions

la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	And if it happens, if you put something on that relieves the pain of the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The two thumbs that arise from the hands of some people by chance are all fleshy,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and by chance there is part where there is bone, and never is there a nail,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	And none of them are born in the root of the joint, or their birth is on the contrary side of us two.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	It is born neither here nor there, for it does not move at all.</start_of_turn>
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and that which is born at the joint must, by chance, move there.</start_of_turn
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the size of that which is furnished is slight, in part contrary.</start_of_turn>
