Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	The fire cautery instructs the patient to let the hairs grow long and even at their root. If they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady until they grow.</start_of_turn>
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.</start_of_turn
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.</start_of_turn
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The sudden pains that ensue must be brought about by birth, or by wound, or by fire cautery, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If it is possible to bear that pain, if it must be so, let it return to its natural form
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two bands or cloths soaked in rose oil, which will not stick;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two pieces of soft lead, until the wound is healed, if possible.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	The fire comes to neither of its two with the palm, if it covers that burn so that it must.
Des vils	The swelling comes to neither of its two with the palm of the hand, if it covers that burn so that it must.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The swellings are blood vessels filled with melancholy fluid, which come in greater numbers with greater pain in the limbs
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more often accompany those who work and travel, than those who remain at rest and who are idle.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	You must not give the patient any purgatives or enemas of any kind, and then afterwards the rest of the treatment.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment with iron is as follows: two methods. The first is with sponges, and treat the black wound;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other method is to ligate the vein and treat it all with force.</start_of_turn>
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The size is as follows: arise the first the hot water bag very strong, until the swelling is not too thick,
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	Then strain the limb of the patient from under the buttock to the part below the knee.
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	Then grasp the vein in one loop, or two, or three, of a large size,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then remove the black blood from your hand from the one end to the other, as much as the patient can tolerate;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	And then bind it, and command him to keep himself well supplied with nourishing food that is black in color;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	And resume the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The limbs of the patient are as follows: if there is moisture in the limb, open the limb of the patient, if there is hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put out or bathe them, and loosen the limb of the patient until the blood becomes red, and swell the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you have no bath, if you burn with fire, and then cover the vein from the shoulder to the elbow, or in the part below the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then after, cover the skin with oil, and gently massage the belly part, until it opens when you feel it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you see it red and black, and when it enters or the skin seems like a white thread.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then press the wound downwards, until it is level with the skin, and then put it to the oil again lightly
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then press the wound downwards twice more in a space of two fingers; then massage the skin over the belly until it opens,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then take hold of the limb at the shoulder, as you have done; and the other limb at another place, as you have done first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then take hold of another size, or more if you have need; then grasp the limb, and take hold of the shoulder bone at the other end
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then draw it up and hold it until the other size; then grasp the limb and pull out the shoulder joint piece by piece until it is all out, then hold it
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you do not draw it and lift it, if there is a strong double thread at all times,
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And the arm and the shoulder, and between these two bones there are sometimes cysts [fluid-filled sacs]. Take hold of the hand from one side and from the other, until they are gone;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And keep that it does not move, for if it moves, if we cannot hold or lift it, there comes harm to the patient.</start_of_turn>
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have finished treating it, if you put out the limb from the wound covered in soft wool in wine and rose oil; and cure it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the patient's limb is contracted and tortuous and bound together, and it is not right, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	If you think it is necessary to force it out, do not cover it up; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The form of fire from which we cover the head if it is crooked, do not pierce it, only cover the wound; ...
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	...it is of great curvature, for if it were subtle, it would cover the vein, but be large as we have said, and this is the form:
De la voinne civile	From the civil vein.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is enclosed in the leg, in hot regions where herbs and trees do not grow, and in the earth where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and sometimes it occurs elsewhere in the leg; this comes from corruption which comes from the decay of the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	if it comes from the marrow of the bone and upwards, enclose between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	and if there is a great inflammation in the leg,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	Then the limb changes place, and the vein becomes taut as a plant root.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the bone is opened, if it is suspected that you should wrap around a piece of lead from one and a half inches up to two inches, and hold the limb steady,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	leave the lead in place on the limb, and every time that it is necessary to move it, if you wrap around the lead, and the new piece.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, if you must break off a part, and wrap around the rest, and do not cover it in its root, until it is completely healed;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	For if you grasp it firmly, if it returns to its socket, make an incision and discharge or extract the foreign body, and do the same with the disease.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Therefore it is necessary that it be treated from the beginning and until the end, and that nothing be left or retained
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and never is this vein when it is treated with five palms of length, or ten
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and one must pierce it from the tenth palm of its length, and when you grasp it firmly, if it returns to its socket, make an incision and discharge or extract the foreign body, and do the same with the disease.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	If all is ready; and whether the material which is within be evacuated, bring medicines to the limb without delay, and cure as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	Never has this vein hands rained, even when it bursts open at the joint of bone, or bone on bone,

Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	From worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is known in our land as "buffalo sickness," because it often happens after a buffalo attack.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	it is a small wound that arises between skin and bone, and runs throughout the body, from head to foot.</start_of_turn>
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and causes great pain throughout the body, as long as it breaks the skin or moves, and spurts blood.</start_of_turn
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is accompanied by the discharge of various humors, such as blood, worms, pus, and worms or abcesses.</start_of_turn
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	And doubt is cast on his malice, for when he goes through the flesh, and he ascends to the head, and he comes to the marrow,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	And thus he returns inwards, and destroys the marrow; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see him cured and treated, if one cannot force him until he goes away:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	then you must certainly bind his limb above and below with a strong and well-made bandage.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	Then put your hand over and above, and if it moves into the flesh, you will not find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	Then put your hand over and above, and if it moves into the flesh, you will not find it, if the fire cautery is done above, while it is burning;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does is when it scorches the oil, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or close to the oil, if you grasp its bristle with your thumb, then put your hand over and above, and if it moves into the flesh, you will not find it, if the fire cautery is done above, while it is burning.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	And you must instruct the patient to use various medicines that can dissolve the harmful humors that cause these ailments.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And he should abstain from eating rotten food
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	From the pain that comes from wind-sickness.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and is a pain that comes in the limbs,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	And thus if it moves from limb to limb; and I saw that which I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I went to a woman who was sick and saw that her arm was swollen at the elbow;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and later it grew like a worm on her shoulder
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	more swollen than anything, like gold that has been cut in two;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	The pain departs from that limb and seeps into the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	The pain departs from that limb and seeps into the shoulder, and then often returns corrected throughout the body, as far as the opposite arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then I heard that it always returns back into the body, as I saw it.</start_of_turn>
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I wondered how it managed to move from limb to limb, because I had never seen anyone with this disease before.</start_of_turn
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Whatever be the reason, I advise that when pain in a limb compels a movement to another part,

Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see the healing of this ailment, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said,

Des saiettes	If the doctor gives vent to these winds, if like foul pills, and pills of serpin, and like other things of that sort.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	If the doctor gives vent to these winds, if like foul pills, and pills of serpin, and like other things of that sort.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	If the doctor gives vent to these winds, if like foul pills, and pills of serpin, and like other things of that sort
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And those which have joints at a right angle, and those which have tongues, and those in which there are pieces.

si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in the thumb, forearm, shoulder, pelvis, ribs, intestines, bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it happens in none of these limbs, and it is a sign of death, that I will tell you later, I will teach you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	If you suspect that the extraction of this arrow is dangerous, for death often follows in multiple conditions.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	If you notice no other sign of danger and the arrow does not penetrate deeply, grasp the shaft and cure the wound.</start_of_turn>
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	When the arrow pierces the bone and breaks the skull, seize the lever above the brain and pull outwards.</start_of_turn
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	This is when the scrotum and testicles swell, the testicles become sore and dark, there is vomiting of bile, inflammation of the tongue, spasms and a mixture of senses, vomiting of bile;

Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it is bent or crooked is that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were caught on something hard, do not break it open.

saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Indeed, doubt arises that death is imminent.</start_of_turn>

And the sign of the dislocated shoulder that never lets go is when it jumps out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns pale, and breathes high and quets the food away.</start_of_turn

Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I have already told you, because of that which you do, there is often a bruise or swelling at the root of the wound.

Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And they drew an arrow from the throat to a crest, and the Arabic arrow had a head like a nail.</start_of_turn
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I wounded the barbarians, and outwitted them until I drew it out, and they were all safe.</start_of_turn>

et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and remained there for three moons altogether.
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then it grew so large that I could no longer hold it together, and split it in two parts, and could not bear it any longer;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	and I continued to toil and devise various methods, until I finally took hold of it with strong pins,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	According to what is said at the end of this chapter, until I tell you otherwise, I shall restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And they judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it therefore, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Or as you have said about the quality of the extraction of some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	If you place your remedy upon that which I do not speak of, for it will not understand me;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but you will know my masters understand me well in many things, and on that which is present and lacking,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	find nine works, and nine instruments, in the descending order of things that arise in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that the sponges do not arise from members or are made of fabric except in the way that I shall explain.
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	Or by the left hand or by the right hand, or from another side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	Or by the left hand or by the right hand, or from another side; and that which is pricked by the nails or which enters, is a splinter embedded in the flesh, and it must not be pricked ever again.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	Or by the left hand or by the right hand, or from another side; and if it does not prick now, if you leave it as long as the flesh is swollen and painful, celebrate the escape;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	Or by the left hand or by the right hand, or from another side; and if it is fixed in the bone, and cannot be pulled out, if you leave it for a while, and move it every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And thus it jumps, and if it does not jump, if you pierce through all the bones under the skin, as long as the wound is stretched, then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the cartilage is fractured in the bone of the shoulder, and goes up to one of the bellies of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and does not go out any of the accidents that I have mentioned to the patient: if you do not cure it immediately, but leave it as it is until it is equal after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the cartilage comes up to the surface, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the splinter is not firmly fixed in the bone only, and does not go deeper than the surface,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the splinter is not firmly fixed in the bone only, and does not go deeper than the surface, and remains lodged in the patient for a long time, it will cause pain and discomfort.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is firmly fixed in the flesh and cannot be extracted, if it has been there for a long time, as I have told you; then cure the limb until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	If the splinter is embedded in the flesh and cannot be seen, if the owner has tried everything;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	If you suspect it, if the pain has no visible cause;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	if you do not see it from the wound, and from the depth of the arrow.
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	it is neither bone, nerve, nor vein, if the wound is great;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	if there is an ear in the arrow that holds it in place.
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	If the bone is entangled in the flesh at the joint that you are touching,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or tear the edges of the wound as long as you can grasp it.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	but take care not to break the bone, only grasp it more tightly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you do not do it once, if the limb is already swollen, then grasp it more firmly, for the extraction will be joyful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the discharge of blood opposes you, if necessary mix what we have said about the treatment in this chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and take care of the incision of the nerve and the vein, and put something there as you would to prevent the arrow from slipping out with danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or tighten or loosen it, firmly or gently; and hold the patient according to the form in which it was when the arrow struck him
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for that is the greatest help of all, and if you do not know how, look at what he shows you
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The bandage comes from another place, or it reveals nothing, or the skin is swollen in that place where it is seen or felt secretly.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	So be it then, as long as the nails can grasp, and then withdraw: if the jump is now made.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, if you twist your hand round and round, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then withdraw it.</start_of_turn
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot be driven out, if you leave it in, and then begin the extraction once more until it comes out.</start_of_turn
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	If it is from an arrow that it comes, hold it at its full extent.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	If it is from an arrow that it comes, hold it at its full extent. If it is administered with a pointed instrument, do so immediately, if it is administered indeed.</start_of_turn>
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	if the point of the arrow gets caught in the socket of the instrument; and then hold it tight,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is hooked, if the instrument has a pointed end to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the wound is surrounded, if you must, copy all the surrounding flesh or the venom is in it, if you must.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	Then treat the wound as you deem appropriate.</start_of_turn>
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the wound is close to the chest, foot, belly, bladder, or ribs, and is nearby, and you must cover it over, if necessary.</start_of_turn>
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and take care to cover the vein and nerves, and then extract them, and then suture the wound, if necessary.</start_of_turn>
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And the cure, as long as it is sound.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the tweezers with which we treat the wounds is similar to the beak of an osprey, and thus is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are various kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the wound
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the blunt end is also like the quill of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	For to stop the bleeding at the tip of the arrow, if this is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	For to stop the bleeding at the tip of the arrow, if this is the shape: the form of a clamp to stop and to hold if it is like this.
des voinnes dou cors communes	it is common for veins to bleed when they are opened or cut.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	When a vein is opened or cut, it is common for blood to ooze out of it, or to bleed profusely
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	It is known that: the bats which follow the ears, which are called "herbech".
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the veins which are in the temples appear.
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the veins which are in the armpits, which are called "aspires".
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein which is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein which is at the back of the neck;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	And the two thumbs which are either curled inward or extended;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	And the two veins which are raised above the mouth, these are the veins which are called «augeherich».
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	And the two veins which are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins which are commonly seen are two in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the cephalic, and is with the left costal, and they call it the people 'chief vein'.
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the middle one is called 'fast', and is composed of the cephalic and basilic.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and they call it the people 'vein of the head'; and the basilic if it is on the left or right coast
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and they call it the people 'belly vein', and is above the navel,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And it is that which we already said, which openly appears on the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the saving limb is the vein which is between the auriculacle and the annular, and if there are two rains;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the limb and where the heel and the toe are two veins: one if it is from the cubitus bone down to the little finger side,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second vein which is at the ankle on the outer side; and the vein which is called the “nessus,” which is in the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other limb are two veins close to those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The blood of the veins that are behind the ears helps to expel old blood and discharge;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the blood, as I told you, is that you raise your head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and wipe the body or the veins are rough; then tighten the patient’s neck with a screw,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	As long as the veins open behind the ears towards the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	and if you feel the pulse throbbing in your ear, it is a sign of a dislocation.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet and pierce the vein down to the bone, then keep your hand firmly on the upper part of the vein,
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	then make it stretch and stretch until it is about an inch and a half long,
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then the strain and the pain, as long as it is whole;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already said concerning incision and cautery or first book.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The blood of the two arteries that are in the temples, if it is like an ancient emigration,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and swelling, and usual vomiting, and at the root of tears there are pus;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the like of a healthy man, if it is as I have said.
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	And it is that the patient stretches his neck, so that the veins open widely;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and he feels the pulse of his thumb and then marks with his index finger;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then he inserts the needle through the vein in his upper arm, and holds the lancet from his thumb
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	And hold the vein high up, and the cuff, as you have done in the last three veins, and do the evacuation of blood as needed.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then loosen the patient, and place your hand over the vein for an hour, then put on a bandage.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Then bind the limb firmly, and leave it so until it is healed; as we have mentioned previously concerning its swelling and extraction, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The blood from the forearm is just as valuable as that from the cephalic vein in old diseases, and in migraine, and in redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And if the patient strains his neck by twisting, as when a vein bursts;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called the "fosser", which is like this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And put the point on the vein, and hold it in your hand, or on something else, and let blood spurt out as much as you see fit;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then deliver the patient the neck, and bind the vein until it is firm and never let the work be done with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Whatever, I say that the flames must not be too strong; and the same through, because the bone is close, and by chance breaks the flames when it is subtle.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The blood of the veins that are in the armpits helps to hold the eyes, and to the touch, and to the redness, and to the swelling in oil, and has diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their blood is that if the patient strains his neck by twisting from side to side, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then, and so forth, and let the flame be long and strong, because there is no hair.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	If the flame is stubborn, by chance if it breaks; then draw out blood, as much as you are able, and then bind it up tightly, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	Blood from a vein does not weigh like water, but it is necessary for wounds, for thirst, and for ailments of the face.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	If there is a migraine and redness that comes on the face, and even when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and if the patient’s head is stiff, then strain their neck with your left hand,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	And take the fire subtly long, and hold it in the space between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the vein does not open easily in this way, and if you do not begin it will not be cured now.</start_of_turn>
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too deep into the wound, and do the cure of blood according to your need, then bind it up for the night, for it is often restored in the morning.</start_of_turn
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the fire:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The blood of the armpits helps to relieve swelling, to initiate the blending of medicines, and for many diseases, and for swelling, and for corruptions, and for herpes, and for tumors.

De la sainie des leivres	Of the blood of the veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the upper limbs helps to clot in the mouth, and to corruption of gums, and fissures of the lips, and toothaches and pains.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And if the quality of the blood is to make the patient sit in front of you, and strain his neck as I have said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the liver, and look at these two veins, one of which is on the right liver and the other on the left
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and you will know them by this that they are black, and that there are small black veins running into them.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	then take both of them, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt,

De la sainie desoz la lengue	If the greatest bone of the shoulder is displaced towards the front, and in the same way make four veins which are below and behind, because this is a foolish method.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	If the greatest bone of the shoulder is displaced towards the front, and in the same way make four veins which are below and behind, because this is a foolish method. The evacuation of blood from the armpits and the tongue helps to staunch the bleeding from the head, and this is at the widening of the throat, and there are diseases of the eye, and there are diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the sick person is that if the patient lies between your hands before the sun, and he holds the tongue, and looks towards the outside of each chest, he sees a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Healthy then, both of you, and do not go too quickly, for blood is in the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins which we commonly cauterize are usually healthy in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or if you prick at their root with a mild, blunt flame, such as a twig or olive branch, as with trenchant cuts, and is called "anesil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are large and subtle according to the size and distance of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The flame of fire is soft if it is mild, and is broad as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And has master to open the great veins full of blood that contain great blood and trouble.</start_of_turn>
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive flame.</start_of_turn>
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more pointed towards the tip, and is for the healthier veins, or where there is little yellow blood.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The blood of the basilisk, which is one of these veins, helps to cure diseases such as sore throat, or swollen neck, or pain in the belly; or swelling of the abdomen.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the patient to remain calm and quiet, and to be wary of the artery that is nearby.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	If he tears the artery, and blood flows out, if the bleeding is contained, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and must not be excessive with the fire, but must be held back as if with nails.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	If the basal part does not open visibly, if you must extract it, and bind another in its place.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or if you wish to avoid bloodshed, or if you wish to hold the limb still in its place: it will open visibly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the scapula burns away with the flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you see that the limb of the blood vessel is coming loose, if you must extract the limb, that you touch the limb until you know the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then sign the limb with your finger, and then lie the arm flat on the flame-filled vein.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And beware that you do not cut into the artery when you see the limb swell, for it is an artery: stop immediately.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it swell up like the urine of a child, and it is without redness and swelling, take it that it is without an artery:</start_of_turn>
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	haste thee then, and put your hand along its length, and then rest your hand if it does not bleed, for many times it has happened;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	The arm lies loose, and lets it be, and do not move the patient; and if there is fear, and do not move until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If it hangs loose and does not bleed, and the physician is not present, if the artery bursts open, for the shoulder joint recoils; grasp it without touching it.</start_of_turn>
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	Take a sponge of physician, and put it in, and take one of the halves and bind it securely to the other side.</start_of_turn
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If it does not bleed, that is good; but if it does not stop bleeding, as we have said, powders that stop blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the swelling does not cease in multiple situations by the small leak of the wound, and the possession of the hand of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The blood from the vein helps to cure the disease from its head downwards, and from the bones outwards.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basal and cephalic parts, as we have said before;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is necessary for the sensation that it should arise from the nerve that is below, and if it is not too deep, and it finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	And he swells up, and his sanity is gone, by chance he cannot recover;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And thus the nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in some place by its subtlety, it is certain that you must loosen the sanity from the instrument that hinders it; and withdraw the nerve from your hand.</start_of_turn>
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, if it has a long loop.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The blood of the cephalic vein helps, that it attracts blood from the head, and helps the veins;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is proper to cauterize with the olive flame or the mirtin flame, for these are the safest of all veins, for they have no bones, nerves, or arteries.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, one must inquire cautiously the first time, and grieve nothing if it does not succeed the first time, and we repeat the procedure.</start_of_turn>
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And by chance, if it happens to swell to some people the first time, although it does not succeed the first time, it does not grieve anything.</start_of_turn>
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your thoughts.</start_of_turn>
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you must know about health is that blood is not merely withheld for the sake of preserving health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and for avoiding future ailments.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	or in the cephalic, facial, and basilar veins
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and it must be done at the commencement of the menstrual period, and after eating, when the signs of repletion appear
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	And if one must strengthen the first joint or the third, after one and a half or two hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The nourishment that is administered for illnesses has no definite time limit, but whenever there is a need for joint or nut, at all hours and at all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and one must not strengthen the children until they are twelve and a half years old, women who are breastfeeding should only consume four months up to seven times
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	One must not strengthen the ones who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when anyone appears to be well, in whatever way, if it be known that he has swallowed a lighter bladder stone,
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if it be known that he has swallowed a lighter bladder stone, if it has caused the veins to swell up and obstruct the intestines from their natural flow as principal symptoms;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	neither from excessive eating of meats, nor from vomitings, as much as from fevers, for these things cause a weakening of the spirit.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if after such a colic passion, vomiting, and great pain in the belly, many women, journeys, cares, and anxieties follow, and whatever virtue, or from weapons or poison;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then subtlety the humors, if they are not great, by foods and drinks and medicines, if you have any at your disposal.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	Then mix with baths, if nothing hinders you, to subtilize the blood.</start_of_turn>
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and give them baths of vinegar or oil, as we have said before.</start_of_turn
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep them from work, from food, and from luxury, and from similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	And so the patient should keep his arms bound and joined, and let the patient's shoulders be higher than the collar that he is wearing, and wipe the patient's brow once or twice.

que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	The wound did not take and failed at the cutting.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that flee like strings to the surgeon, and some that are full of windiness,
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	when one puts on the flame, if one takes it away again, one cannot open the vein, and that is what is often the case.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if the wound is too great, because of this one must be warned in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If the vein bursts the first time, that is good; if not, if you start again, take hold of the limb or the patient, for if it does not swell.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	If the limb swells and the patient sighs, leave it for an hour or two, and do not bind the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	By chance, there will be swelling; do not enter or bathe, then restart the bleeding if it stops

Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	And if you see the wound inflamed, if you do not immediately stop the bleeding, put on a patch of lint soaked in oil, for it softens the skin of the wound, and is much more effective in this limb the oil that the lint.

et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, do not put anything else on it, such as aloe or mastic gum dissolved in vinegar, mustard, or the like.</start_of_turn>
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Many times there is swelling and blood appears at the root of the hair: put your hand there, and if you feel the root is loose under the pressure of your hand, that is a bad sign.

Do not put anything on it that we have not mentioned, for by chance without an artery; but make it dry again with another dressing, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	Treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.</start_of_turn
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if it is black, leave it to fester as long as it is red; and if you see it large, leave it until it is delicate; and if it is too thick, let it cool down.</start_of_turn>
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is proper for the one who is calm and strong, and has the skill of extracting blood, to make the wound larger, and let the flame be large.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and keep it healthy more than before, and must do it healthy by cutting across, not by pricking.</start_of_turn>
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of bleeding is useful for the evacuation of blood and the compression of nerves, and is worth more than if the blood were long rather than wide.</start_of_turn>

And for the one who has the cold towards blood, it is proper to give soft bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if it is faint, give two or three parts of blood.</start_of_turn
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant. et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter of fainting, for the evacuation of the stomach.

ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	if it is crooked, extend the limb widely, for that would be bad.</start_of_turn

Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is stained in leu of the vein of the head because it is composed.

Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The blood of the armpit of the right hand is worth for all the diseases of the liver, and this is the manner:

Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The blood in the left hand is worth the disease of mice, and do the same as I have said before for the upper part.</start_of_turn
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The blood of the sophene is worth for all the diseases that are outside the body.
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	if like maladies of the marrow, and retention of flowers, and disease of the veins, and swellings of the legs and old wounds, and similar diseases.

And if you keep it healthy on the bone, if you guard against the nerves that are over-moistened, and the limb remains whole just as if you were grasping; and let the flame vanish.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot be kept in place, if you reset the bone in water, and let the vein drain well.</start_of_turn

ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and make the other side equally serene.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The pulse of the sciatic nerve is at the ankle of fire, and its blood is worth the pain of the groin, when it is for blood that is hot.</start_of_turn>
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its blood is that if the patient is between or in water, and strains under the ankle, there are three fingers of blood to twist.</start_of_turn
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise it does not open; and if it does open, in all the ways that you can, and by crossing,
