Des sainies de ventouse	From the ventouse.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventuses are made of horns, or hair, or glass; and the suction must be performed according to its manner: either by cutting and drawing blood, or by cutting alone.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this cutting suction, which is done by cutting, is performed in two ways: either it is with great heat, or with cutting only;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and the suction which is done by cutting and drawing blood is done in twelve pulses of blood.
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	Since the previous sentence has not been translated, I am unable to provide a translation for the given line.
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the other on both sides of the collar; and the tongue hangs loose below the chin.
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the tongue hangs loose below the chin; and the tongue hangs loose over the teeth;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the thumbs are swollen; and the ankles are swollen;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	And the swellings of the joints of the calves; the swelling does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the marrow.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	And for this reason, it does not matter much, if as we make a bleed from a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	it is only to be administered, without fire or heat, in no disease that comes from repletion, as long as all the swellings are drained.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of a disease it is necessary to perform a ventosation, or by custom, if the physician deems it necessary at the beginning or at the end of a month, or at any other time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For some, when they must breathe, if they have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	And for some, when they must breathe, if they have a heavy head, and if they have swelling and redness in their face, and in their head, and at the throat, and dark urine;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and such people have a discharge of blood in their mouth, and their tongue is swollen, and they vomit blood.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And for some, when they must breathe, if they have a heavy head, and if they see blood and foam and mucus and pus and other things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	When these signs appear, and even if it is only lightly moist, we command the patient to wind after two hours.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	When the blood from the wound helps to relieve the pain in the head … that comes from the pus, and it must not be left until after the evacuation of all the flesh;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	is better than the evacuation of the head wound
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and must not be left until someone who is pale in complexion or who has chapped lips is left in charge, for they make great discomfort;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And for this reason I advise you not to use it on patients suffering from cold or severe diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And for this reason I advise you not to use it on patients suffering from cold or severe diseases
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The suction cup on the collar is in lieu of the blood of the chief and the bile, and for this reason it is worth more at the end than at the beginning.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and with a tear of the carpal tunnel, and with all, and with distension;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it is necessary to urge [the shoulder] slightly, for if it is held too tightly, it will impede obedience or cause pain in the flank or belly or side.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	And the windings as two costles about the head cause pain in the chest, and pain of the head, and swelling, and strangulation, and pain at the root of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it is in place of the blood of the vein; and it is necessary that you command the patient to express his hand to put it in, that he does not cut the artery, and does not see blood oozing out.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The vomiting of the stomach is if there is a disease of the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and is in place of the health of the two upper teeth.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The winds of the spleen are harmful to health, coming from heat and congestion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The winds of the spleen are as harmful as two veins of the arms,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because they draw blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and commands the patient that he should not feel too much pain, because it is known that marrow is soft, and bones and arteries are fragile.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The wound on the buttocks is of great importance, as it brings swelling to the foundation and causes diseases. It is therefore necessary that the vacuum be large and of fine mesh, and that it be well applied; for if it is too subtle, it will break and cause great damage.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The wounds on the legs swell widely, for they draw blood from all parts of the body, and cause ancient pains of the rains, and of the marrow, and of the bladder, and soften the flowers; and are in connection with the joints of the thighs and the calves, and all of them weaken the body after a long time, and cause vomiting in various positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the vacuum is that you must first empty it, and then put it on quickly and firmly, and move it equally, and do not cease doing so until you see the red liquid and swelling, and open the wound of the blood; then close, and put the vacuum back on, and take care of the body, for there are such people who have a very tender temperament, and clear pores: if you must cut once only, it is better to make large wounds and a deep incision; and do it gently
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if it is not large, it is sufficient to wound it thrice: the first time to uncover the great blood vessel.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if it is not very thick, it is sufficient to wound it thrice: the first time to uncover the great blood vessel. And when our veins swell with blood too much, too little, if we only suffer once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And when our veins burst with blood, if we repeat it often; and if it is not thick, if we pierce too deeply, and if it persists, if it is perceived that the wound is too deep
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	it is appropriate for those who have thick skin and tough hair, and who have large pores, that you remove the scabs of oily and dissolving salve.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is in this state, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkinseed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	If it is in this state, with ivy oil, or cypress oil, or daisy oil, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is large and cold, if you take amaranth oil, or balsam oil, or rue oil, and the like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the skin is tight and has large pores, you must not put any oil,
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	But it is necessary to wash afterwards with vinegar of roses, or cold vinegar, or vinegar of violets, or vinegar of cucumber, or vinegar of porcelain, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And if there is moisture in the mouth, if it lifts easily, or with vinegar of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.</start_of_turn>
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And if there are excess phlegmas, if they lift from old wine, or vinegar of rye, or decoction of ivy or chamomile, or other similar things.</start_of_turn>
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it does not suffice to keep the hair dry beforehand the bath, but one should wait an hour or two after the bath; and do not sleep after the ventosation.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And it must be known that it will worsen when it is exposed to the wind and when it is windy.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	When it is exposed to the wind and is windy, it becomes angry and swells excessively.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	If it grasps cold things, such as pomegranates, onions, lettuce at ease, and the like;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and fat from fish, mutton, and moist meat.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, if he takes syrup of honey, and scented wine medium, which is between elder and nettle, and fennel, and mint, and poppy seeds and small birds and marigolds;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and when he feels a draft, he must drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and must give some warm clothes neither silk nor cotton before or after, in order to comfort the principal parts of the body;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	or be careful not to give it to those who are already hot from drinking.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The wounds which are made with a cutting instrument are those which are made upon the liver, and upon the spleen, and under the kidney, and upon the belly and the buttocks and the thighs and the heel, for in these members no wound is suffered upon the outside.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and are made only to draw blood from the limb to limb,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	for as when we place it on the bones when we do not wish to bleed; to remove the viscosity which is in the limb, as when we make incisions on the belly and the buttocks to make the limb flexible
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it relieves the pain, when there is swelling or a bone is fractured, so that by its attractive power it pulls out the swelling, or removes the bone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	And thus it is held aloft when placed upon the liver and upon the spleen when there is retained wind.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	These winds are administered empty, with the exception that sometimes they are mixed with oil; and never are they administered with fire, and never are they plain with water that boils over
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	if there is disease of the pleura, and in such a manner we fill the wound with hot water or water in which there are herbs that cover this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the wound administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And there were twice the width and half a palm of barley, and either cost or twisted round about a mile and a quarter, as when pushing out an awl.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	Or be of rain, sweat before if it does not harm the patient when putting it on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and there was in the middle a bar of iron or wood, to put a bandage in place,
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and in these there are great and small according to the maladies and the extent of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And must we put this sponge on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	grip the handle of the crucible or rather the lining, and put it into the sponge through the hole that is in the sponge,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	If the burn is at the root of the wound, it does not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	Then place it over the limb, and must either over the hole that we have mentioned, so that when we look, if there is any vapor, and if the burn is over, the wound is evacuated by the ventouse.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And keep the dressing as before, and repeat it often, if you are able.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the ventouse, which is administered in the case of pleurisy, at all severity, there is no vein or hole, and it is only administered when it is full of liquid, and is placed on the limb only for a moment;
et c’est li forme:	And this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	There are no other means of support except for members or where one cannot put on bandages because of their small size, like books and gums, and similar things.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and for bones that are stripped of flesh, if it is necessary or not, and other things of that kind;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and if you find bones that are soft and clean without any wound, take them out;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	And put one nut in a sweet water, until they are familiar, and do not have anything in their bellies.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	And then either ligate the vein and the veinlet, then wipe the limb until it is red, and put on the bandages.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	When they are full and relaxed, and can be moved, if it is possible to put on a suction cup, put it on, for this is better afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If this is not possible, if you lift the limb easily, and then with water, wet thoroughly, and then squeeze it out;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the limb remains too long after the wound has healed, if it is wet, such as a drape of linen in cold water, put it on until the wound is stretched out.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	If the wound is gaping, put on a piece of broken glass or bandage, and similar things, until the wound is stretched out.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you take half of a roasted pea and leave it on the limb until it blisters, if you stop it now.</start_of_turn>
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you have more pain, take other wounds.</start_of_turn>
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	If the limbs do not yield to the touch, rub the limb with fresh blood, or insert a needle until the limb is whole again.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	then hold them up, and as soon as they feel a little blood, if they swell up;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they groan, if you sprinkle over some alum and lead powder, or ash, they will groan now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This is the end of the text.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is restoration of fracture and displacement.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Listen well, my son, for this chapter teaches you things that no former book has ever mentioned, that no letter has ever recounted.</start_of_turn>
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	Therefore, in our land, this science is strange, for I have never found any good example of it.</start_of_turn
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	I do not know anything about it, except what I have learned from the books of the ancients, or what I have learned through study and experience in my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	And thus I have described in this chapter what is contained in it, and I have abridged it at the end, and I have made clear the forms of the instruments that are mentioned, as I have done in the previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, I say that the prologue of this book and the chapters contain the essence of the word and that the learned man who reads and comprehends them will find true understanding, for those who have been proven to be skilled in this noble art and have learned it well.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture, dislocation, torsion, or stiffness occurs, if you are to restore the health of the patient on one side and the other, without any other thing, except for weakness of the limb, infancy, or old age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	Or if the tension is not too strong, or too cold; mix cold broth, that is to say cold broth of herbs, and charcoal of oil and ivy, and do not drink wine, do not eat any fatty foods, and do not eat too much meat which fills the veins of blood, until you have no doubt of the depth of the burn, or of the swelling of the limb; if the patient recovers before the next morning, he must repeat the treatment that he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to restore, if you must know that you must nourish the patient with foods that make great nourishment, or that have viscosity, such as barley cooked in broth, peas, and beans, fish, eggs, cheese, and fat, and similar things.</start_of_turn>
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For at a part of nourishment, rest returns muscle and more easily breaks the fracture.</start_of_turn>
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that bones broken in various places and decrepit ones do not mend well by themselves according to their nature because of the drying out of the limbs, nor those that are too brittle, like bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but there is no remedy, keep the fractured bone still, that is, firm tension which has arisen and unites the limb together, until it is as strong as before; and do not move it in any way, for because of this it is necessary to nourish with great foods, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are of various kinds in many ways.</start_of_turn>
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the skull is different from that of the limb, or of the bone, and I shall tell you in this chapter all the ways of fracture.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go only skin-deep, and others by cutting, like the size of a needle to write with.</start_of_turn>
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small tear.</start_of_turn
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And at the elbow there is its own vessel, and its proper instrument in restoring it, according to what it remembers comes to its aid.</start_of_turn
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And it is known that the fracture of a bone is when its limb is bent, and opens well by force, and some with the pressure of the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twist or touch, and the patient does not feel much pain, there is no fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have twisting, or fissure, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you do not know with certainty whether it is twisted or broken, but only that the hand is moved, but put on medicines that will come afterwards, and then strain it now subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And wounds that burst outwards go to the marrow, and are the joints' marrow, it is necessary to put them back in their place equally, even as after an abscess.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if after an abscess it comes, if you leave it without attention, until the abscess is calmed;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then put it straight in the limb as you would do with a bandage and without haste, and wounds that have burst outwards must be restored more easily than those that have pieces; then the strain, as it should be after that.</start_of_turn>
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	and if in the bone there are broken pieces, if it is hands or feet, or at the hand if it is a small limb, or at two strings, or at a string and at the hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	And place the limb according to its natural form, so that when the parts of the limb break, remain by all means the augmentations in their places as before, and keep that by your work no wound or pain should come to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And adjust well the joints of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well with the hand if you think that it is not well: if the limb is well stretched, and is not strained too much, do not press as those who make it come by their work to cause swelling and contraction of the limb, as we have often seen
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	When the limb is at rest, if the patient is very painful and does not move it, neither waking nor sleeping, neither turning nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	...and make sure that the limb is completely still, so that he feels no pain at all.</start_of_turn>
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, if he is not already at rest, you must make him lie still so that he feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and keep him perfectly still, so that there is no more turning around when he recovers.</start_of_turn>
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And the quality of a broken limb is as I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The fractures of the limb are diverse in small and large size and in shape.</start_of_turn>
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small limbs, such as bones of the arm and forearm and similar: if it is necessary to cover them, wrap linen cloth tightly and loosely;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	For large limbs, such as bones of the thigh and leg: if it is necessary to cover them, use a wide and strong cloth, because the large cloths embrace the whole great limb, and strain it everywhere equally, if there is no crease;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then lie down comfortably, that is to say two or three times according to the limb, and strain your hand one palm up to the end, then go under the break and strain less, than the break then pull out one palm of the break.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the limb one palm up and down, as much as you take a great part of the limb again, then take hold of the other limb and turn the shoulder back in place over the limb that is broken;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then raise to the lower part of the break, and strain moderately, not too strong nor too weak, as we said at the first hour above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then put between the layers of cotton wool or cloths, as many as you like, then bind all around with thread, and then put your stakes well made above, if there is no puncture or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or puncture, put above something calming the puncture, and which supports the swelling, and leave it in place for a few days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then strain on your stakes, and be of half of a broad cane resting securely, or of a staff from which you make needles, or of horsehair, and be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that when one puts the splinter in the fracture, it should be a larger and wider one than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	And be as long as it is convenient for the limb in its entirety or proportion.</start_of_turn>
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then is strained upon the splinters as you did at first, and then suspend under a thread of silk as soon as possible, if as at the first upon the fracture.</start_of_turn>
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	The more narrow it is enclosed, the less; and it is necessary that the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, and be of flax.</start_of_turn
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the threads are thick, as I have observed in the works of fools who bind them with linen cord too tightly, this is a great error, for the cord will not be even if it is too subtle, and it will hold only if there is between the nail and the shoe a space less than two nails.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	If the patient is scorched by the nails after the stretching of the limbs, if you put on stockings of linen or coarse cloth, so that it does not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a splinter, and the bone is fractured, I will tell the cure of that later.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And the wounds which he cannot restrain must be stripped off from these bones to break them first in order.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is large, it is not possible to place the bones inside except after five or seven days, or more according to the severity of the wound which comes out;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and when the old plaster is removed to restore the fracture, dislocation, and torsion: take some flour which is held by the walls of the mill, and mix it with a lot of eggs, and put this composition, not too liquid nor too thick, and use it.  This is the common method of restoring the fracture in various situations, and even for women and young children, because it is neither too harsh nor too rough.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plastering which restores the fracture and dislocation and torsion: take three barley grains and linseed and acacia and asafoetida and gum arabic and mugwort, and mix them together; mix in half a barley grain of mirre and aloes, and half a barley grain of alech; and grind them up together; mix them with a lot of eggs; if the patient’s complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it is made of good materials and will quickly restore the broken bones, and is worth more than many homes.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Other methods of immobilization are worth considering: take mustard and vinegar, mix one part of each; mix myrrh and aloes, mix eight parts of each; mix acacia with five parts of each; mix arnica with ten parts of each, and grind thoroughly, and confit with vinegar or plenty of eggs, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Other methods of immobilization are worth considering: take mustard and vinegar, mix one part of each; mix myrrh and aloes, mix eight parts of each; mix acacia with five parts of each; mix arnica with ten parts of each, and grind thoroughly, and confit with vinegar or plenty of eggs, and administer. Take new lint, moisten it in oil and put it on the wound. This dressing will not restore health, but it is good for soothing post-burn pain, and will properly relieve pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Other methods of immobilization that restore fractured bones: take dried fig leaves and terrestrial poppy leaves, grind them together, and make a dressing.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Autre méthode d’emplaustre à la restoration de la brisure de l’os et pour amenuisier le reste de l’apostome. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de fois, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se le membre est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another method of immobilization for the restoration of a bone fracture and to reduce the remaining swelling. Take root of vismalve, chamomile, violets flowers, wheat flour, and one part of meadowsweet; grind, and mix with wine, and if the limb is swollen, mix with moist coriander water or plain water, and use.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras in his book does not put anything on the broken limb to restore it except for some wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between two things not too soft not too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen recommends placing something dry and warm upon the affected limb to restore it, such as myrrh, aloes, incense and the like, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of dressing that is valuable for both pain and swelling: take mugwort and chopped onions, or pine resin, beeswax and smear them evenly, and broil them, and make a poultice from them.</start_of_turn>
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then loosen a little later, and take care that the patient feels no pain, that the bone is not broken; if not, loosen it by hand today.</start_of_turn>
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the limb, or swelling, sense rest or inflammation, if you rush, and loosen it, and place the limb in its proper position now; and take a light bandage, and a sponge of sea salt, and plunge into water, and raise up the limb, until the swelling ceases, and the pain is appeased.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then leave the limb rest for an hour, and put on dry cloth, soaked in water or rose oil, and bind up with a nut, until you are certain of the healing of the burn;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And rest the inflamed limb, and if the pain persists, then bind it up again, and give a little support, and do not restrain it so much that it suffers; and be discreet until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that the abscess is inflamed, swollen, red, and painful, and that it returns again after you have placed it and bound it, as you did the first time, then you must repeat the procedure.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	If it does not recover in the limb what we have said, if it does not subside after two, three, five, or seven days; do not leave it for twenty days, as we have seen, until the inflammation has subsided, and approach the closing of the wound slowly.</start_of_turn>
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Therefore the more restraint you must exercise than before, and nourish the limb; as I said before. And if you see that the limb is drying out more than usual, do not apply poultices;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Arise then, for indeed the water is hot and stinging, every time you touch it, and this be it from every third drop, and split a little of the skin.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Hence in this work, when it is necessary to stretch out the limb, and the fool has made a mistake, that he should return the limb without violence: this is bad, and if he does it carelessly, I see nothing but leaving it loose and doing it right away.</start_of_turn>
des diverses manieres de brisure	from various breaks
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many kinds of breaks, and various figures, and the causes are diverse.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For there are fractures that are made by percussion of a spear, and the collar of bone is split right up to the syphus which is the socket of the bone, as if made by a nail or a fist; and for this reason this kind of fracture is called a "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	When the spear pierces the bone from the underside, and is called this kind of fracture "absolute"; and is the wound of these great or small fractures.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is embedded percussion, or fissure or split of the bone, or dislocation of the shoulder or fracture of the bone, or other similar things.</start_of_turn
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a burst vessel, which approaches the gut that is adjacent to the bone, or it is on the bone, this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that is close to the bone as thin as a hair, and the tear is small, it is called a "capillary" wound.
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if a wound is made by a pierce, or by cutting, or by something similar, and it makes the bone marrow enter, and the limb is swollen like when it is boiled on a cauldron; if there is an opening in the bone between the teeth.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this often happens with those who have soft bones, as children;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And there are many such breaks in these ways that small pieces break off from them as in stars; and I will speak of them later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know of all the ways of breaking due to the subtraction above them, the inquiry into tentatives, and the corrupted flesh which is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary appearance is known by that which when we have discovered the bone, and we wipe on it, if there appears a black break.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, take care of the patient’s condition, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, extension, and swelling, and fever, and the eyes to become pale and flushed, and other similar things in various situations, if you cannot do otherwise
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	If you do not see an imminent mishap, and you hope for health, if so, commence the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When you come to the aid first, and it is in sweat, if so, it is necessary to obstruct the bone before the fourteenth day over the muscle that you must support.</start_of_turn>
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	If it is in this state, if you haste to obstruct the bone before the seventh day over which the cloth of the bone is corrupted, then comes the accident that we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	If the bone breaks down to the cloth that covers the brain, if so, you must make a perforation in the fractured part: and it is that you take hold of the patient’s head and uncover the bone in all the ways that you can, and on the figure of the wound more severely than you can.</start_of_turn
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if blood comes out at the uncovering of the bone, or at an abscess, he should use what he can to prevent it, and you should fill the wound with wet cloth soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And keep the wound closed until the abscess is calmed, and be sure there is no further bleeding; then start to bind the bone securely, which is done in two ways: one way if the tail of the fracture is narrow in front, and the other:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then there is another fracture more extensive than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And thus if you have several different-sized lesions, some wide and others narrow, and some pointed and some blunt, and in an easy matter, without bleeding the head,
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is firm and hard, if you must pierce through it, do not pierce it too close to the bone, but must leave a space or circle above the point, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you must make several of these holes, for if pieces of bone come out in the place of the thickness of the bone, if you make holes too close to the test, they will break through the bone. And this is the form of the two methods of drilling holes:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing through the bone quickly are that you put one hole on the bone, and turn the screw until you feel that the bone is pierced; then put the hole back in another place a little later, and do the same all around, and close the incision between the holes, making it more subtle than you could, and gently, as we have said, until you have moved the bone from your hand or from any instruments that you have like pincers; and keep your hand away from the brain or the jaw.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have perceived the bone, and treated, if it is possible, reset the socket which is loosened from the bone to all other instruments that are similar to an incisor, but it is necessary that it should be more firm and subtle than the other incisor.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	If it remains loose from any small bones, teeth, if the bone is slightly loose from any instruments; then cure the wound with sutures and bandages as we have said
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of treatment is that of the Galenicians, which is more useful; and the load is very great, and this is its word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a portion of the bone, either where it is fractured or broken, so that when you have uncovered that part, put on gloves and grasp the handle of this incisor lens, for this is its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	Do not bore too deeply from one side, for the part that is jagged in .ij. costae lies over the bone; then place a little mallet above, so that you can easily break the bone all around, and take care of the cloth that is beneath;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is open to the bone, if the bone is easily broken, because we must break the bone well soundly, and cautiously.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if a bone breaks without piercing the skin, it is only slightly fractured from above; there are small pieces [of bone] which, if necessary, can be removed with a rasp of various sizes, to bring about the greatest possible healing, according to the work and the nature of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If there is a great deal of razing beforehand, and after that more subtly, and it does not cease to do so until it is well done.</start_of_turn>
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In some other capillary and subtle fractures, it is necessary to provide the cause according to its location; and this is something that is not usually known to anyone who has studied this art.</start_of_turn>
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the swelling is discovered, you must take as much as one drapeil of lint, according to the quantity of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another drapeil doubled in two or three, soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first drapeil; and do this more gently than you wish, that you do not suffocate the swelling, then administer further lint, and do not tighten it more than is necessary to hold the wound in place only
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and leave it for a while or two, until the swelling subsides, then remove it, and administer medicines such as licorice root, oatmeal, and incense powder, and herbs; and from these things make a powder, and put it on the wound, and administer adequate medicines without biting.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And beware that the wound be perfectly closed, that you leave neither the opening nor the stitches undone, for when the stitches gather on the skin of the head, if they are torn and become loose, it brings great harm to the patient; for when one places upon the surface of the body anything that bites, if it does not desist downwards.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Beware then, if no other misfortune befalls the patient, as we have said, if there is any doubt or suspicion.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if there comes forth no other evil than through the medicine we have placed upon it, that some part has its virtue, then you must know that you must take a part of honey, and two parts of rose oil and glue one with the other; and put it upon the surface of the body.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then comes the treatment in various ways, as long as he is sane.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Then come the treatments in various ways, as long as he is sane. The veins that are never broken in the joints, or one by one, because these are bones; and when they are cartilaginous, they do not break, if not by swelling or twisting, and then they are well again.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of these parts is broken, if you should happen to bite your little toe or pierce the bone of the limb, and put the break back into its place at your index finger and at the wrist, as long as it does not recover according to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and make it gently, and beware that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the fracture is in the upper part of the limb and cannot be brought down naturally, as is often the case, you must assume that the limb is fractured at the root of the bone like the head of a club.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	If the fracture is three-fourths of the way up, if you do something else, and do not hurry to restore the limb at once, you will be mistaken;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after seven or eight days, when the swelling of the wound has subsided, when the limb is brought to its proper position, and you attempt to cover the fracture with linen, if the fracture is in this part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you must bite another part of it, if the fracture is there; and let the attempts be so violent that they fill the hole in the limb.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And they say that no restorer should mix the threads in the burn, and each one must die. Under no circumstances should one or two goose quills be substituted for threads, and if there is much snow cover, and the wind blows, and the patient is suffering; do whatever you see fit.</start_of_turn>
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	If blood clots come to the surface while you are working, if you put some lint or gauze soaked in rose oil, or some alum, on it.</start_of_turn
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if after that the abscess does not come away, put on a plaster of hempseed meal, powdered incense, confirmed with the yolk of an egg, then put on light bandages, and do not bind too tightly.

de la routure de la mandibule	Of the root of the mandible.

It is appropriate, if the fracture is in the distal part, to bite your right index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is in the left mandible, if you take your right index finger of the hand, and touch the fracture lightly, and hold it in place with the other hand by force, and keep it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is displaced in .ij., if you must administer extension of .ij. parts, as long as they are even.

If movement of the jaw comes loose, or if there is displacement, if the teeth are strained by a golden or silver or silken thread, then put a broken mandible cerate on and put over it a double drape; and over the drape put a large well-made staple, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the mandible, and tie it on the tooth that you wish, and command the patient to rest, and eat soft foods.

Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if postmortem comes, if it is as we have said many times before.

de la forcele	because of force.</start_of_turn
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The strong force breaks several times before, over the shoulder, and if it breaks in two ways: either it is broken and loosened in three, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And if the break is when the wound is facing downwards, have two assistants; one should hold the arm that feels the strong force; and the other should extend the limb towards the part; then set the break even, so that it forms as it should, and there is neither appearance nor movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient. If you do not manage to push back the head of the shoulder, because it comes out of its socket, you must know that the patient lies groaning on his belly, and put a cushion under the shoulder blade, that is, the middle rib, and support the shoulder from below, until the bone of the shoulder is raised.

et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and seems like a scoop, and is not very deep, and be as wide as it seems appropriate, according to the size of the bone and the condition of the work; and has two holes, as you see, and one is large and the other is small, as is the course of the wound that you made when you treated the bone.

de la brisure de l’espaule	Then resume the displacement, if you see that it is necessary, and hold and leave it in place until it is restored; and it is usually restored in about 26 days, and less in most homes.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement. de la brisure dou pis	And if a piece of the bone bends forward, and not a little, if it persists, and the bone, do as we said at the bursting of the forceps to calm the abscess.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The piece is never broken in the middle, but this happens often; but it often breaks from excessive force. And when it is broken in the middle, if it is declined to the side, and causes the patient great pain, and loss of appetite, and vomiting, and sometimes blood, and breaks the bones in the fracture, and makes the marrow visible.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that if the patient lies quietly on his back, and places one cushion between the scapulae, then press the scapulae, and assemble the bones of the two ribs with the hands, and slightly put each in every way that you can, until the bone is as it should be; then put on patches and bandage the area with fine salt, or other soft matter, and cover with a cloth, and bind the fracture tightly, so that it does not move; and turn the limb round on the back, and stretch it gradually, and give the patient something to drink every hour, and if it loosens, because of corrosion or swelling that comes to the limb, or pain or abscess, if you are in a hurry, and loosen it, and scrape off the patch, and address what has come from the way of treatment; then remount the patch and bind tightly until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of the fracture of bones
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Bones that fracture do not come forth except behind the loin and at the head downwards; and they do not bend forth except because they are glassy; and one feels them well at the inquiry of two fingers.</start_of_turn>
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the restoration is that you must set the fracture equally, as it should be. And then put on the bandage, and bind with a strap, if you have need of it.</start_of_turn
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of bones is downward, if one feels great pain and swelling, just as if of blood, because the bone is pointing at the membrane; and there is swelling, and vomiting, a great quantity of blood, which is a great grief, and they have put a great burden.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if any of those who say it should administer food that swells the belly, to push back the pangs of hunger.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, for after these things have been eaten, they do not go away unless they have already begun.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have already begun, if they are well.</start_of_turn>
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that there is no need to put on stockings on the limb for its swelling, because it is similar to reason; however, there is doubt that the stocking will not collect the superfluous matter from the limb because of its weakness.</start_of_turn
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that on must not cover the limb with coarse linen soaked in oil, but put on bandages between the ribs to measure an even inch of the circumference, then either cure with the cure for pleurisin, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure from the bone that points the rib, and there is doubt to the patient, if you must cut on the broken rib, and you must put in instruments to keep the breast steady; then you must cut the bone slightly and drain the pus, and then sew the two layers of the wound, if it is large, and treat with sponges, as long as it is safe. And if an abscess comes, if you put on wet cloths soaked in rose oil, and put on the limb; and treat while the limb remains in position, and do not move the ribs or it will be broken, as long as it is safe.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the collarbone.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never comes a sudden break of bone from the collarbone, and often it rains; and the same with the spine.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to anyone, and you know if he will be well or not, if you see his hands softened and limp and dead, and that you cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, if you do not feel it. Such is death in many positions, and if you move them and feel well when you strain them and point, it is clear that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if we put a cure on it.</start_of_turn>
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if something like this happens to the spine, and you know if he will be well or not, if you see his feet are softened and limp, and if there is an accident which is in the hands or on the back, with a sudden gust of wind and vomiting without wanting; and when we have soothed him on his belly, if he vomits without wanting. And when he is soothed on his back and he sees himself spitting, if he cannot. Such is death: if he does not work in his cure.</start_of_turn>
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	If this mishap does not occur, then the matter is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	If this mishap does not occur, then the matter is lighter. If there is swelling, put on a rose-hip ointment or egg yolk oil until it is calmed; then put on a comfortable and absorbent dressing, and bind it with a thread, and instruct the patient to rest; do not lie on that part where there is pain, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
