Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If bones break, if you cover on it like this; and unite the edges of the wound, if it is large, with a splint, then bandage with lint, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "shaft of the arm", if it is to the left of your hand, and put it equal to the other hand at your side, then put on the dressing and the bandage, if you need to; then strain it, and if there are broken bones under it, if you notice it, unite them, and cure the wound until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the fracture of the thigh bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	When the thigh bone is fractured, and if so, if there is no sign of improvement at the head; and if it persists, there is a long-lasting pain, bending forward, and comes to the patient pain at the limb, swelling, and bursting of that which was fractured.</start_of_turn>
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that if you extend your hand over, as long as you are over the fracture; and grasp what is fractured and the figure of it; and if the fracture is only at the head, if you make it equal to the natural figure.</start_of_turn
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it bends inwards, if you make the patient sit on his belly, until the restoration of this fracture is apparent.</start_of_turn
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set them even, if you put on the support, then put on a ball of fat or cork, and tighten the bandage, so that it does not move; and use the liquid dressing to support the costae, until the ligature is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his side, or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if the swelling comes, do not touch it, until the swelling subsides; then put on what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and tighten it as it should be, if there is no other mishap; and that is the remedy.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	De la brisure de l’ajutoire.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	From the dislocation of the shoulder
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And there are two ways to reset the dislocation: one is to take a fist full of moist earth and form it into a cone-shape; then put the limb over the fist, as far up as the armpit, and hold it there with the fist under the armpit; then put the hand over the break without any weight or support from the attendants; then put the patient’s hands together, so that the break returns naturally.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	Or the other method is to hold the patient’s arm at his collarbone, and bind the hand to his neck, and command the attendants to hold the part above the break at his hands, and the other to hold below at all the joints, and extend the chest towards the part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	If the extraction is too violent, if you strain it, that is to say pull out the splinter, above and below, extend your thumbs to their ends. And if the splinter is close to the head of the shoulder, you must put in the middle of the glen of the shoulder and the other towards the elbow, pull out the splinter; and if the splinter is towards the elbow, put in lightly, cautiously, as long as the splinter is level on both sides, and on the elbow; then put the splinter back in place if possible, and strain, because if you do not strain, the aftershocks will come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If after straining there are aftershocks, do not strain for more than thirteen days. Put on soft linen and rose oil until the aftershocks have subsided; then strain, and keep the position of the strain as if you put in the pad on the splinter. Then assemble the arm on the shoulder and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; put on the bandage and strain the shoulder and the arm, so that the arm is in its place, without any hindrance, or that the bone is not fractured.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is not moving, use splints, and on the splinter put on a splint wider and stronger than the others, and put between the splints two spaces, and let one splint be as long as the splinter extends two fingers; then strain on the splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter about the splinter, more strongly and less loosely
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If you see the swelling of the bones and the stretching, as we have said, when restoring the limb, if you doubt the depth of the wound, if you leave it to join up until seven days, as we have said; then look carefully for two days that the swelling does not increase or that new swelling does not arise in the limb because of that. If the swelling persists, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	If no such thing occurs, if more than two days have passed, and the patient lies on his back with his hands on his stomach; and give the assistant a cushion made of even wool, and look for an hour or two to see if the limb is not moving or the ligaments are not softened; if the swelling persists, as we have said. By the power of medicine, do the necessary; and give the patient the food that we have before mentioned, in small amounts; and when he begins to recover, let the assistant and the limb be taken out in forty days. And when they are taken out, administer a bath and external medicines for the appropriate part. And if the fracture is loose and bloody, leave it undisplaced for one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	And if the fracture of the arm is displaced, leave it undisplaced for one day or two months.
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of three bones, which are called the «flescle», because one is small and the other is large; and the small one teaches the pouch, while the large one is hollow, towards the little toe; sometimes the large bone fractures alone, or the small one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small bone fractures, the restoration is light, and the healing; but when the large bone fractures, if the healing is bad, it is more painful than when they fracture together. If only the small bone fractures, if the limb is slightly extended, and made even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large bone that fractures, if the limb is more tightly bound; and is extended over one cushion, and the pouch of the hand is held higher than the other, and the small one is lower than the other, and the patient is crossed over himself, and the cushion is in front of him higher than the patient suffers no pain; then extend the limb from the hollow part to the wrist, or to the elbow, and another assistant to the other side. And then set the limb in its proper position, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the burst (dislocation) it breaks into pieces, if you place some support in its place, and if there is no slippage that pricks like before, you shall not be able to restore it to its place; then leave it as it is and support the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the burst (dislocation) it breaks into pieces, as I have mentioned in the singular case; take the cure
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if at the commencement of restoration, if pus come out after the incision of the apostemes, put glue. i. drape it with cerote made from rose oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; and bind. i. drapelet by under, until the apostemes have ceased to bleed. Then bone the cerote, and put in place the powder of the mill with abundance of eggshell, because put the stars, and let the star of the burst be more firm, and a space more wide than the others; and wash that there must be between the stars or arms in several positions: whether the burst is in one of the bones, or in two; and is strained more on the burst than elsewhere, and all the days less by loosening, as I have said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths that are on the burst be soft and moist, neither too hard nor harsh; and let the thread, which is strained, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And reward the limb and the ligament after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	If other evil accidents happen to the limb, as for example itching that happens to the limb, then you must raise the limb with hot water until the itching subsides; and then leave the limb still. Then start the treatment again, and if the joint is softened and the bone is loosened, and similar things, if necessary.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	If you take care that the nourishment does not come to the limb because it is too stiff, then you must soften it somewhat, and leave it for a while, until the nourishment returns, and then strain it.</start_of_turn>
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of these things that we have said help the patient, if not until twenty days have passed, or even longer, then you must hold his hands to his collar, and keep his collar even, and be careful of movement and vomiting, and sleep on his back; and give him nourishment every three days, or every four, according to the compositions and temperaments of the medicines.</start_of_turn
de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	The nails on the back of the hand, and we have had two breaks there, often comes from fractures, and comes no more than once or twice.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the hand is broken or fractured, if it is suspected that the bones are fractured, the patient should sit comfortably forward; then place the hand on a wide bandage, and the physician should extend the fractured bones and align them properly; and put on plaster and bandages, if necessary; and put on a splint as needed; and be covered with a sheet of linen.</start_of_turn>
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is on the outside of the limb towards the belly, make a loop of cloth, and command the patient to hold it against the fractured limb; then pull from a long bandage, and be supported by a splint as large as the limb, and strain, if necessary.</start_of_turn
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is outward, if you command that you place a pin above and another below at the joint, so that the hand is overextended and straight, then hold it firmly around the hand, and staunch the bleeding between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break does not come from above or below, if it is at the elbow, if you command it to be even; and you stretch with the thumb, and if you see that you must place a pin straight, small to lift the break, and it does not move; and if the break is elsewhere, as in the index or any other, if you command it to be even, and you bind it with the two hands which are after; or you bind them all together, holding the wrist, or you place a pin upon it, as with a pouch; and take care in the restoration and arrangement of the cautery burn, and secure what comes out, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	and if the break is outward, if you command that you place a pin above and another below at the joint, so that the hand is overextended and straight, then hold it firmly around the hand, and staunch the bleeding between the two.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the thigh are often fractured, and it is well seen when it turns before and behind; and the restoration is when it is bound with thread beneath the fracture and above.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	The patient lies on his face, then extends his limbs equally; and it is when the fracture is in the middle of the bone
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the fracture is close to the head of the thigh, if either of the two ligaments above the fracture is torn, and the other ligament below the fracture. And in the same way if it is close to the knee, and in any case either the ligament above the knee or the extension below; then put the thumbs of both hands against the bone until it is in its natural position, and then put on the bandage and bind it securely, without leaving any space.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess above, if you leave it quiet and return to your work and your cure; the suture is made in haste.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap around the wound, that is, a bandage doubled in half, in two or three places, and keep the excess taut, then turn the limb until the nails reach the root of the nail, and pass between the heel and the limb, from below the knee, and pass a thread long between the heel and the limb, from below the ankle. Then turn on the limb and on the heel the bandage, and put on the external dressing, and put a stay on the bone of the limb; then use up the remaining cloth between the limb and the heel with coarse cloth to make equal the tension, and begin to tie forming two or three turns on the dressing; and the more you go up on the dressing, the less the strain. Then take out two or three stitches that you had passed between the limb and the heel, and tie two stays that are below, then return to the initial position of the thread, until you see that the pain has gone away; and the strain, if it does not move from its place, then leave it alone, and do not cause any other abscess or swelling or anything similar.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if there is swelling, if it comes loose, and you address that which comes, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, it is necessary to remove them; and if we are unable to do so, we must cut the limb and drain the pus; and cure as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the bone broken in this way that it can be put into place without causing pain to the patient, as in the arm and the shoulder; however, in restoring it that is done, it does not cause any harm to the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And sometimes the bone is restored in a day, or less or more, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groin area.
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	There are often breaks in the groin, but they often bleed repeatedly. And if it breaks, it is no longer just a tear, or a perforation, but there is pain, and blood, and this is well known.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is set right, do this: put the rounded peg back in its place until it is well assembled; then put the stuffing in, and put a round pin in if you have need of it, and hold it as it should be held; then restore all the arrangements that we have mentioned before, as for example incisions and other similar things; if you put in every mishap that it should be put in, as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	And if it is set right, do this: put the rounded peg back in its place until it is well assembled; then put the stuffing in, and put a round pin in if you have need of it, and hold it as it should be held; then restore all the arrangements that we have mentioned before, as for example incisions and other similar things; if you put in every mishap that it should be put in, as long as it is healthy.
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	And if it is set right, do this: put the rounded peg back in its place until it is well assembled; then put the stuffing in, and put a round pin in if you have need of it, and hold it as it should be held; then restore all the arrangements that we have mentioned before, as for example incisions and other similar things; if you put in every mishap that it should be put in, as long as it is healthy. Saiches that are in the limb have two bones; one is called the "mustelz" and the other is called the "foscile"; and there is a break in all parts as it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is the same as that of the arm, and the work is all the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if two bones are broken together, the limb will be twisted from every part.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if a subtle bone is broken, it will twist forward.</start_of_turn>
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if a great bone is broken, it causes great pain, and one can see it well; and it twists downwards.  Therefore, bring extension, and make it even, and bind the bones evenly; but nevertheless, if the break is severe, and there are many pieces, even if the extension is smaller and lighter; and align it as best you can.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, if you take.ij. strips of coarse cloth which will embrace the limb from one side to the other, and be as long as the limb from the knee to the foot; then cover with.ij. cloth.i. bandage above and below, and bind firmly in the middle, and with this binding the limb will not slip downwards or upwards, and that is good; and let no one administer any more drugs whose length is greater than the limb, and which may cause stiffness, and put on the limb a support to prevent movement, and do this cautiously at the break or in the case of an injury; and move each part of the limb, in order to see if there is any swelling or other accident; if there is swelling as much as before.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the fracture of bones due to violence.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, fracture does not arise; but in bones of violence, fracture never comes alone, and there must be two together; and there is no other cause of death but certainty and fear.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture in bones of violence, and you see these bones pushing against each other, if you put the limb so sick on the earth, as if it were falling from the sky, and then put your limb on the ground, where the bones are raised, then press the limb until it returns to its place; then put on the dressing and bandage, and put some small weights on the belly of the limb, and hold the limb firmly, and as soon as the limb has healed, wrap it in bandages, and other things that you must provide.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when two or three days have passed, if the limb is loose, because you will find the bones equal, whether fractured or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there are two fractures, restore them as we have said; then place at the fracture a splint of the length of the fracture, and make it wider; then place a bandage over that wound that I have mentioned. If there are three or more fractures, break them; then place upon each fracture a splint according to its quantity, enveloped in one layer of linen, and strain the wound over the fracture. Make it firm over the top of the fracture and over the abdomen of the fracture.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	Remember also the other things that I have mentioned concerning other fractures, as we have said; and treat each case as it should be treated.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the clavicle bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the natural woman’s bone is broken, if she sits enlarged, then she inclines towards the lower back; and let her be held by behind. Then fill the belly with cotton, and put as much in as a stone; then draw out the woman, and keep her back and front; and immediately jump the cotton out until it reaches the entrance of the natural woman; and bring back the bone with the stone. And when she sees her piss, if the stone is in the cotton, and when she has pissed, she returns, and in this fashion make seven days or until the fracture is restored: if the fracture is restored, and you see, take a bladder of herbs and bind the belly with a bandage, and keep the bladder in the natural woman; then blow in the bandage until the bladder is expelled: the natural woman will then restore the fracture; then fill her with cotton and leave her for a few days until she is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	When the wrist bone of a man or a woman is broken, if you restore it as we have said concerning the thigh bone; and these fractures which arise from excessive study and use are not concealed by anyone who knows my book. For a fracture signifies in many cases the right way of restoration: understand then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the arm, when it is broken, take a goose beak and bind the arm; then cover with bandages, and leave for two days or until the arm is healed.
de brisure avec plaie	Of sudden with wound.
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	In the case of sudden fracture with wound, even if it is great, as with the bone of the thigh or the shoulder or the like, that it be set right now, as the symptoms which we have mentioned bear witness.</start_of_turn>
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is well closed, if the vitriol has been retained, if you have nothing else, then repeat the restoration of the fracture in this way, or that way, for if it does not come, after these measures.</start_of_turn
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the swelling comes, if you must leave the restoration until the swelling has gone down, as long as the swelling is appeased, and do not touch either the third or the fourth part, for you will otherwise cause a worse accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if a bone breaks suddenly, it appears above like a wound discovered, so you must cautiously hold it at a slight extension with your hands.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the limb does not naturally extend with your hands held even, if the instrument of iron, which is about thirteen or fifteen inches long, and its width is according to the extent of the wound; for this reason it is necessary at the midpoint that it grasps three or four inches, according to what is necessary in the treatment of a fracture; and let it be round and somewhat thick, so that it does not pierce the limb during treatment, or be placed before, and thick in the middle forward.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	It is called a "palainche" because it is necessary to place the curved limb upon the visible part of the bone; and once it has been placed, let the bone recover, and let the one end meet the other. And if the fracture is slight, and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, if you must cope with the head of the bone, as long as the instrument has possession of it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	If you cannot restore the bone, as we have said, if you grasp with a curable instrument, such as an incision or a hook, at your peril; then withdraw that which is remaining embedded in the bone with rough raspings and fine splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	When the bone is restored, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, it is because it is not in its natural position. If you do too much and force it back into place, then moisten it with black wine vinegar, and do so cautiously; put no cerote or other thing on the wound except oil, as it will cause decay and corruption; then administer stars [medication] when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the dressing all around, according to the size of the wound, and take care that the wound is not strained with the breaking; for many times this has happened to fools, and it has caused the patient to die or become paralyzed or rotten on many occasions; or the inflammation is more mild and soft than the others.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	If the wound is bad or large, and you doubt whether any remedy will help, as we have said, and you feel pain in the place, if it does not suffice to administer stars [medication]; but cover around with a cloth, instead of stars, a firm bandage, and tie. And when you see afterwards that it is swelling more or less than before, when you put on the stars that you put on before, put on healing ointment for wounds, such as ointment tetrafarmaçon and the like.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you bind the limb three times a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be supported in a gentle way that the limb can move slightly without causing discomfort
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If the limb persists, and cannot be reunited at its proper place, because there are small bone fragments, it is necessary that you close the wound with great care, and remove all these fragments which cause pain
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	If a fistula arises in the limb, or any other kind of corruption, if it is necessary that you cure it, according to what is said in the preceding chapter. And when a bone is fractured, and is open on the limb, as the bones of the thigh or shoulder, and other large bones, if you do not treat them, for many times death comes from this; leave them alone until they heal naturally; and then cure the wound if you wish; or leave it alone
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Hair that comes out with the scab
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Hair that comes out with the scab comes out many times after the heat of the wound, even when it is close to the joint, and is a helpful sign that the limb is recovering naturally.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then that it is fresh: if you give astringents such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocoll, acacia, and similar things, that you do not take any of these things, or all together, and mix them with a strong wine or with eggs or with oil; and put them on the wound in bandages, and strain it well, and do not remove it from the hand for days; and then remove it, and start another one, until the nodulation is bony; or you strain it on a well-made piece of leather; for the property of leather is that it will harden all the swellings under the limb; and if the nodulation has already turned into hardness just like stone, and it is necessary to harden it, if the swelling above is complete, and remove the excess; or do not remove it at all, until it is bony, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Weak limb after care
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone is restored and the limb is weak and limp, if there is any discomfort: sometimes because it was too tightly bound and was not loosened enough; or because there are too many bands, and it cannot move smoothly; or from too many wounds; or from excessive movements, not in its proper place; or because there is too much blood in the limb, if it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is to make the patient walk and keep the limb firm, until it is multiplied in him; and give him baths, and make him cheerful and comfortable; then put a poultice on the limb, so that the poultice attracts to great nourishment, and the wound often bleeds profusely until the nourishment comes to the limb; and bring it back to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The limb is twisted after the seizure.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bones are broken open, and the limb is deformed, though it retains its natural movement: if one does not believe the fools who say that the limb must be broken anew, and many have suffered from this in our land; this practice is blamed, and great evils result from it; often the patient dies. Though if the spasms and the torture are fresh, if you believe they have arisen from warm water, or soft herbs are cooked, like ivy leaves, root, and melilot, and similar things; and you apply an emollient plaster, like fine powdered aquaintance well made, and take the nourishment of ivy, and confit with beef fat or oil of sesame, and apply plaster on; or you take fat figs, and grind them with horse dung, and similar medicines that appease the bowels.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And never is the bone fractured by continuous rubbing with moist hands. And either give the limb gentle movement from the outset.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the dislocation is swollen and hardened, like stone, and requires iron wire, if you cover it up to the bone, make a slight incision; and put padding and a bandage on the wound.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	And so begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to no more, if you can now restore the limb to its proper position.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if it is late, if it has swollen already, and by chance if one attempts to reset it, there will be prickings at the root; for because of this one must not move it while it is swollen: many times it has brought on vomiting and other pains.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	When this has happened, if the patient is still able to move, let the patient rest; once the swelling has subsided, warm and oil the limb, then gently restore it to its place. Cure each limb individually as needed.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters concerning dislocations of the shoulder joint to the end.
des mandibules	Des mandibules.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	The mandibles. For the mandibles are loosened and the dislocation of both is as follows: either they are a little loose from their sockets, and softened somewhat; or they are loosened entirely, and hang towards the chin, and cause the saliva to flow from the mouth that it cannot hold it back, cannot close its mouth, and engulfs its tongue with the words.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, if it returns by itself in several positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is entire and accompanied, if you must, immediately restrain it, and do not delay;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such a manner that the minister holds the head of the patient, and behold the eye that is beside the pocket of one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the mandible in the mouth, if the dislocation is of three parts; and the other hand must be lifted up, to make them even; and command the patient to soften his mandibles and move them from all parts.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And behold the eye that is beside the pocket, until it returns to its place.</start_of_turn>
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is grasped, even if both mandibles are together, if they arose from hot oil, as long as they remain lightly; do not force me to restore it, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are restored equally, and the patient’s mouth is gently closed, if you put on moist cloths in a circle made of rose oil and wax, then bind them loosely with linen thread.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And the patient lies on his back, and his arms are placed between two cushions, so that they do not move forward or backward or to the sides, do not attempt to force, but take hold of the limb gently, until the pains are past, and note the teeth;
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	Then gently move what you see lightly, and do not work too hard to open the mouth to eat or drink, until the jaw is well numb and healthy.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	If the teeth do not return to their place at a single hour, and are not otherwise converted, fever and nausea will ensue, and sometimes vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	When you see this, know that it is a loss; and often death follows in eight days.</start_of_turn>
de la forcelle	of the forceps.</start_of_turn>
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot grasp deep within without causing displacement, and is worth nothing when removing it, and it is often felt.</start_of_turn
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu formant a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if the patient lies with his back on the ground and extends his arms; then press the limb towards your palm, and it will return; then place the dressing and bandage on it, and hold it in place; command the patient to rest until he is well.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and in this way the shoulder is reset when it is loosened from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	The shoulder is dislocated only by two means: firstly, that it be dislocated at the armpit downwards; and secondly, that it be dislocated at the shoulder-blade downwards; and sometimes at the top of the shoulder-blade, and this is dangerous.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	It does not come loose behind for the shoulder, and does not come loose from the nerves; and many times it comes loose downwards towards the armpit, even among those who have little flesh, for at these jumps there is great pain; among those who have enough flesh, there are jumps with pain, and they return with pain.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes there are percussion or fractures, and the shoulder is inflamed by a thick abscess, and care must be taken that it is not dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is necessary that you be certain that it is actually dislocated; and once you are sure, then you may begin treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	Dislocation is known when the shoulder is displaced toward the back, and the difference between the affected and healthy shoulder will be evident; you will find between them a noticeable separation
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and at the top of the shoulder you will find a socket, and when the shoulder is pressed against the socket, just as if it were a bone; and the patient is unable to raise their arm to its original position, or to move in any way
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and thus too, if it is dislocated upwards, if not hidden, because you will see it immediately;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this manner of dislocation is not without force to restore it, when it is new, or when the limb is painful.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the way is to take hold of the painful limb with the hand above, then put your thumbs under the armpit, and take hold of the joint forcefully upwards; and then the hand must be held and stretched upwards, because it must be set in place.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come as we have said above, if it is to be believed that the patient is to be bathed in warm water; and it is to be given soothing and comforting nourishment, such as a decoction of elderberry and fennel and honey in water, and to be given.</start_of_turn
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then either keep the patient still on his back, and put under the armpit a cushion of linen equal in size, not too soft nor too hard, and put the hand of the shoulder over the cushion, and keep the shoulder joint firmly in place, and treat the painful hand.</start_of_turn
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	And another attendant holds the patient’s head still, so that it does not move downwards; for the shoulder joint returns immediately, and if you see that it remains fixed in this manner, you must rejoin it in this way.
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	And it is that you make it known, that is to say that there is someone who is greater than the patient; and that you take two fingers of the patient’s hand, and pull the shoulder out from the patient’s side, and hold the shoulder up, so that the patient’s arm hangs down naturally.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And another attendant grasps the patient’s hand downwards towards the belly. And if the patient is too light, if you put anything heavy with him, the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And in another way we must remind: if the head of the shoulder is long and firm in the earth, and the arm hangs like a pistol, neither too thick nor too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then if the limb is too heavy or the patient is too weak, but there are coarse hairs on it, and the patient’s hand is extended from the other side, the joint will return to its place without difficulty.</start_of_turn>
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not return through all these things that we have said, if you do this cure: take a fist of three fingers and two palms of the width of a barleycorn, which has the thumb bent inwards to enter between the bones of the shoulder, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lay on the head of the sufferer a drape of cloth, so that it does not touch the patient, and put on his seat the patient; and extend your arms over the patient's head, and hold the sufferer's limb on the patient's arm, and the arm at the wrist, and put the arm on his elbow of a span wide, and stretch out the hands backwards, or leave the forearm hanging down: the joint is now restored.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is restored, in whatever way, if you put on his seat a ball of wool as big as an egg, put on the plaster bandage of powder of wheat, with incense and balm of egg, on the whole shoulder and around, then strain off the seat immediately, and turn the limb on the bandage, and embrace the hand at its collar, and keep the hands still.</start_of_turn>
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is to be known that it must be massaged often, as long as the limb is comfortable, for it will heal more quickly; and then massage more after five or six days, and move it; and if it is stiff and is not softened, if it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is forced out of place by moisture or for some other reason, if you must administer cautery to the two ends, if it is placed before or alongside the cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it does not heal within twenty-three days, and the joint does not stay in place, and cannot lift the arm up, then know that the nerves at the head of the shoulder are compressed or stretched or softened; and that the joint never heals in its place.</start_of_turn>
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the elbow, and the bones, or behind, if it is made by impulse and extension of the arms, and if another bandage is administered; and it cures as long as it is healthy.</start_of_turn
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	If after healing the limb grieves and becomes stiff, if the patient uses the limb many times, until the grief is relieved and returns to its former state.
de la dislocation dou coute	If after healing the limb grieves and becomes stiff, if the patient uses the limb many times, until the grief is relieved and returns to its former state.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	If after healing the limb grieves and becomes stiff, if the patient uses the limb many times, until the grief is relieved and returns to its former state.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	If after healing the limb grieves and becomes stiff, if the patient uses the limb many times, until the grief is relieved and returns to its former state
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must ensure that it is reset immediately and firmly, so that if you postpone it, if it comes back again, you will cause more harm than good; and even if it is at the rear, it is better to leave it than to risk bringing it back in its entirety, even if it is delayed. For it is more painful and dangerous than other dislocations, and often leads to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And if it is possible to restore it, when it is in such a way that you can bring it back, extend your hand with both hands; and let your arms be spread out, and your hands down following the curve of the joint, from front to back, and hold the joint together with your thumbs and index fingers, until it returns to its place
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, if it returns when you double your hand over your hand, and hold from the root of the bone that is loosened.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not return to its place, administer great extension; and if two ministers extend the arm and hold it by two ministers, if it does not move during extension; then turn the arm from the elbow downwards, and having enveloped a double-long and wide cloth.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	And when you see the limb at the joint, if the limb has no oil to nourish the joint, then strengthen the joint, until it returns to its original position
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And when it is in its place, if you put on dry plaster with egg yolk, and the limb is strained, and you bend the arm at the elbow of the patient, and leave it for some days, and then take it off.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is firmly fixed in its place, if you loosen the limb and leave it; if you see that the joint does not move smoothly, repeat the displacement and loosening of the limb, and leave it thus for some days, until it is firmly set; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	If after the joint has been reset, there is pain, and it moves, bathe and rub it thoroughly, and press until it is eased; or put a poultice of fat sheep on the joint, and leave it on for a day and a night, then remove the poultice, and make the limb enter the bath again
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	When it sweats, wipe the joint gently, then put the poultice back on, and then enter or bathe; and do this three or four times until it is healed; and if you see that it has returned to its place.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand. The joint of the hand is loosened, more so than any other joint, and it must be immediately repositioned in its place, even if it is swollen or there is pus.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	If you place the painful hand on a table and extend the limb, and you look at it to make it even, so that it places its palm on the surface of the joint and pulls it until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	However, you must watch if it is well aligned; then put the painful hand back on the table with its palm up, and pull it out and in again.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If the dislocation is at the back of the hand, put the patient’s back on the table, and put your hand over the appearance of the joint. If it returns now, it is well.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, if there is straining of the supporting muscles after the incision, keep the wound open and let the swelling subside in its natural course.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if it cannot be endured, and you do not wish to set it again after a few days, leave the joint immobile.</start_of_turn
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	and do not harm the patient in any way until the hand is softened, and do not attempt to extract anything: except in cases where the nerves are cut, or an artery; for otherwise there is no other remedy but to cauterize immediately, which is better in this case.</start_of_turn

de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the shoulder of the hand.

dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	From the loosening of the shoulder joint at the back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder or neck joint is loosened, or there are several such loosenings, if no cure is found, for the patient’s death is imminent.

Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And often the shoulder dislocates at three parts; that which dislocates at the back is called "gilbosite".
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	If the swelling has arisen from childhood, and there is no remedy or healing to be found, then let it be left alone.

mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have abridged it according to my intention, and I have formed instruments in various ways.</start_of_turn>

et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	And thus too, when it comes directly to these costs, and it is not possible to cure them except by that which comes from behind, as I have said.

Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And it is that thou shalt hold .ij. fingers at the head of the patient of a great arm, and over the pieces .ij. others, and between every finger shalt be a sow and an oz, a palm's length.
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	And between every finger shalt be a hole, or the nail is twisted, and the fingers shall be firmly fixed in the earth, so that they do not move; and between every two fingers shalt be a nail which is turning, so that the nail returns, and there shall be in two returns two little nails of a palm's length, in order to bring back the nail.
